10110{_}1761{_}"Next week there will be a gathering of lawyers," he said.
10110{_}1762{_}"The police will be represented, probably by the Treasury, if the case is thought sufficiently important.
10110{_}1763{_}That chap, Ingerman, too, will employ a solicitor, I expect, judging from his attitude to-day.
10110{_}1764{_}In fact, any one whose interests are affected ought to secure legal assistance.
10110{_}1765{_}One never knows how these inquiries twist and turn."
10110{_}1766{_}"Thank you," said Grant, smiling at the journalist's tact.
10110{_}1767{_}"I'll order tea to be got ready while you're taking your pictures.
10110{_}1768{_}By the way, what sort of detective is Mr. Charles F.
10110{_}1769{_}Furneaux?"
10110{_}1770{_}"A pocket marvel," was the enthusiastic answer.
10110{_}1771{_}"Haven't you heard of him before?
10110{_}1772{_}Well, you wouldn't, unless you followed famous cases professionally.
10110{_}1773{_}He seldom appears in the courts--generally manages to wriggle out of giving direct evidence.
10110{_}1774{_}But I've never known him to fail.
10110{_}1775{_}He either hangs his man or drives him to suicide.
10110{_}1776{_}If I committed a crime, and was told that Furneaux was after me, I'd own up and save trouble, because I wouldn't have the ghost of a chance of winning clear."
10110{_}1777{_}"He strikes one as too flippant for a detective."
10110{_}1778{_}"Yes.
10110{_}1779{_}Lots of people have thought that, and they're either disappearing in quicklime beneath some corridor of a prison, or doing time at Portland.
10110{_}1780{_}I wonder if Winter also is coming down on this job."
10110{_}1781{_}"Who is 'Winter'?"
10110{_}1782{_}"The Chief Inspector at the 'Yard.'
10110{_}1783{_}A big, cheerful-looking fellow--from his appearance might be a gentleman-farmer and J. P., with a taste for horses and greyhounds.
10110{_}1784{_}He and Furneaux are called the Big 'Un and the Little 'Un, and each is most unlike the average detective.
10110{_}1785{_}But Heaven help any wrong-doer they set out to trail!
10110{_}1786{_}They'll get him, as sure as God made little apples."
10110{_}1787{_}"Then the sooner Mr. Winter visits Steynholme the better I shall be pleased.
10110{_}1788{_}This tragedy is becoming a perfect nightmare.
10110{_}1789{_}You heard that fat-headed policeman speak of my face being covered with blood.
10110{_}1790{_}He did it purposely.
10110{_}1791{_}I made a fool of him this morning, so he paid me out, the literal truth being that a branch of that Dorothy Perkins rose there caught my cheek as I entered this room on Tuesday morning--before I discovered the body--and broke the skin.
10110{_}1792{_}I suppose the cut is visible still?
10110{_}1793{_}I saw it to-day while shaving."
10110{_}1794{_}"Yes," said the other, chortling over the "copy" his colleagues were missing.
10110{_}1795{_}"The mark is there right enough.
10110{_}1796{_}Queer how inanimate objects like a rose-tree can make mischief.
10110{_}1797{_}I remember a case in which a chestnut in a man's pocket sent him to penal servitude.
10110{_}1798{_}There was absolutely no evidence against him, except a possible motive, until that chestnut was found and proved to be one of a particular species, grown only in a certain locality."
10110{_}1799{_}"How fortunate that the Dorothy Perkins is popular!"
10110{_}1800{_}laughed Grant.
10110{_}1801{_}"Will your paper publish photographs of the principals in this affair?"
10110{_}1802{_}"I expect so.
10110{_}1803{_}I've a fine collection--the jury, all in a row--and you, making that speech to the mob."
10110{_}1804{_}"Oh!
10110{_}1805{_}Will that appear?"
10110{_}1806{_}"By Jove, yes, sir.
10110{_}1807{_}It was wired off before the inquest opened."
10110{_}1808{_}Grant reddened slightly.
10110{_}1809{_}His own impetuous action had blurted out to the whole world that which Steynholme was only thinking.
10110{_}1810{_}No wonder Furneaux had warned him to go slow.
10110{_}1811{_}Perhaps the little man was annoyed because of his challenge to the village crowd?
10110{_}1812{_}Well, be it so.
10110{_}1813{_}He meant, and would live up to, every word of it!
10110{_}1814{_}The afternoon dragged after the pressman's departure.
10110{_}1815{_}What Grant really hungered for was a heart-to-heart talk between Doris Martin and himself.
10110{_}1816{_}But, short of a foolish attempt to carry the post office by storm, he saw no means of realizing his desire.
10110{_}1817{_}He must, perforce, await the less troubled hours of the morrow or next day.
10110{_}1818{_}Doris would surely give her father an exact account of the conversation between Grant, Furneaux, and herself that morning, and that greatly perplexed man could hardly fail to see how unjust was the tittle-tattle of the village.
10110{_}1819{_}So, avoiding Mrs. Bates, whose fell intent it was to ask him what he wanted for dinner, he struck off along the road to Knoleworth, walked eight miles in two hours, and reached The Hollies about seven o'clock, rather inclined for a meal and much more contented with life.
10110{_}1820{_}Minnie announced that a gentleman "who brought a bag" had been awaiting him since half-past five, and was now asleep on the lawn!
10110{_}1821{_}A glance at the aforesaid bag, still reposing in the entrance hall, sent Grant quickly into the garden.
10110{_}1822{_}A long, broad-shouldered person was stretched on a wicker chair, and evidently enjoying a nap.
10110{_}1823{_}A huge meerschaum pipe and tobacco pouch lay on the grass.
10110{_}1824{_}The newcomer's face was covered by a broad-brimmed, decidedly weather-beaten slouch hat, which, legend had it, was purchased originally in South America in the early nineties, and had won fame as the only one of its kind ever worn in the Strand.
10110{_}1825{_}"Hullo!
10110{_}1826{_}Wally!
10110{_}1827{_}Glad to see you!"
10110{_}1828{_}shouted Grant joyously.
10110{_}1829{_}The sleeper stirred.
10110{_}1830{_}"No, not another drop!"
10110{_}1831{_}he muttered.
10110{_}1832{_}"You fellows must have heads of triple brass and stomachs of leather!"
10110{_}1833{_}"Get up, you rascal, or I'll spill you out of the chair!"
10110{_}1834{_}said Grant.
10110{_}1835{_}A lazy hand removed the hat, and a pair of peculiarly big and bright eyes gazed up into his.
10110{_}1836{_}"Oh, it's you, is it?"
10110{_}1837{_}drawled a quiet voice.
10110{_}1838{_}"Why the blazes did you send for me?
10110{_}1839{_}And, having sent, why wake me out of the best sleep I've had for a week?"
10110{_}1840{_}"But why didn't you let me know you were coming?
10110{_}1841{_}I would have met the train."
10110{_}1842{_}"I did.
10110{_}1843{_}Here's the telegram.
10110{_}1844{_}That pink-cheeked maid of yours nearly had a fit when I opened it to show her that I was expected."
10110{_}1845{_}"You wired from Victoria, I suppose?"
10110{_}1846{_}"Would you have preferred Charing Cross, or the Temple?
10110{_}1847{_}Isn't Victoria respectable?"
10110{_}1848{_}Grant laughed as they shook hands.
10110{_}1849{_}Hart was the most casual adventurer in existence.
10110{_}1850{_}His specialty was revolutions.
10110{_}1851{_}Wherever the flag of rebellion was raised against a government, thither went Walter Hart post-haste by train, steamer, or on horseback.
10110{_}1852{_}He had been sentenced to death five times, and decorated by successful Jack Cades twice as often.
10110{_}1853{_}"I'm a sort of outlaw.
10110{_}1854{_}That's why I sought your help," explained Grant.
10110{_}1855{_}"I know all about you, Jack," said Hart slowly, picking up the pipe and filling it from the pouch.
10110{_}1856{_}The meerschaum was carved to represent the head of a grinning negro, and was now ebon black from use.
10110{_}1857{_}"I felt like a pint of Sussex ale after a hot journey in the train, so hied me to the village inn, where several obliging gentlemen told me your real name.
10110{_}1858{_}Two of them, Ingerman and Elkin, apparently make a hobby of enlightening strangers as to your right place in society."
10110{_}1859{_}"I must interview Elkin."
10110{_}1860{_}"Not worth while, my boy.
10110{_}1861{_}Ingerman is the crafty one.
10110{_}1862{_}I thought I might be doing you more harm than good, or I would have given him a thick ear this afternoon ... Oh, by the way, what time is it?"
10110{_}1863{_}"Seven o'clock."
10110{_}1864{_}"A little fellow named Furneaux is coming here to dinner at seven-thirty.
10110{_}1865{_}Said he would drop in by the back door, and mutter 'Hush!
10110{_}1866{_}I'm Hawkshaw, the detective.'
10110{_}1867{_}He resembles a cock-sparrow, so I asked him why he didn't fly in through an attic window.
10110{_}1868{_}He took my point at once, and remarked that he wanted none of my lip, or he would ask me officially what became of Don Ramon de Santander's big pink pearl.
10110{_}1869{_}It's a queer yarn.
10110{_}1870{_}There was a bust-up in Guatemala--"  "Look here, Wally," broke in Grant anxiously.
10110{_}1871{_}"Are you serious?
10110{_}1872{_}Did Furneaux really say he was coming here?"
10110{_}1873{_}"He did, and more--he expressed a partiality for a chicken roasted on a spit.
10110{_}1874{_}You have a spit in your kitchen, he says, and a pair of chickens in your larder."
10110{_}1875{_}"How did you contrive to meet him?"
10110{_}1876{_}"You're a poor guesser, Jack.
10110{_}1877{_}_He_ met _me_.
10110{_}1878{_}'That you, Mr.
10110{_}1879{_}Hart?'
10110{_}1880{_}he said.
10110{_}1881{_}'Mr.
10110{_}1882{_}Grant's house is the first on the right across the bridge.
10110{_}1883{_}Tell him'--and the rest of it."
10110{_}1884{_}"Have you warned Mrs.
10110{_}1885{_}Bates?"
10110{_}1886{_}"Mrs. Bates being?"
10110{_}1887{_}"My housekeeper."
10110{_}1888{_}"No, sir.
10110{_}1889{_}If she's anything like your housemaid, I'm glad I didn't, or I should have been chucked into the road.
10110{_}1890{_}I had the deuce of a job to reach the lawn.
10110{_}1891{_}Had I ordered dinner I might now have been in the village lockup."
10110{_}1892{_}Grant hurried away, and placated Mrs. Bates after a stormy interlude.
10110{_}1893{_}Precisely at 7.30 p. m. Minnie came and said that "Mr. Hawkshaw" had arrived.
10110{_}1894{_}"Bring him out here," said Grant.
10110{_}1895{_}"Fetch some sherry and glasses, and give us five minutes' notice before dinner is served."
10110{_}1896{_}"Please, sir," tittered Minnie, "the gentleman prefers to stay indoors.
10110{_}1897{_}He said his complexion won't stand the glare."
10110{_}1898{_}"Very well," smiled Grant, rising.
10110{_}1899{_}"Put the sherry and bitters on the sideboard."
10110{_}1900{_}"Say," murmured Hart, "is this chap really a detective?"
10110{_}1901{_}"Yes.
10110{_}1902{_}He stands high at Scotland Yard."
10110{_}1903{_}"Never more than five feet four, I'll swear.
10110{_}1904{_}But I wouldn't have missed this for a pension.
10110{_}1905{_}I have a revolver in my hip pocket, of course.
10110{_}1906{_}One would feel lonely without it, even in England.
10110{_}1907{_}But I hope you can stage a few knives and daggers, and a red light.
10110{_}1908{_}I can cut masks out of a strip of black velvet.
10110{_}1909{_}That girl will have a piece stowed away somewhere."
10110{_}1910{_}The two entered the dining-room study, where the table was now laid for dinner.
10110{_}1911{_}Furneaux was seated on the edge of a chair in the darkest corner.
10110{_}1912{_}His eyes gleamed at them strangely.
10110{_}1913{_}"Can you trust Bates?"
10110{_}1914{_}he said to Grant.
10110{_}1915{_}It was a wholly unexpected question, and Grant answered sharply:  "Of course, I can."
10110{_}1916{_}"Tell him to make sure that no one trespasses on your lawn between now and ten o'clock.
10110{_}1917{_}Close that window, draw the blind and curtains, and block that small window, the one through which you saw the ghost."
10110{_}1918{_}"Ye gods!"
10110{_}1919{_}cackled Hart ecstatically.
10110{_}1920{_}"Why all these precautions?"
10110{_}1921{_}demanded Grant, rather amused now.
10110{_}1922{_}"I'm supposed to be on the very verge of arresting you, and it would weaken the faith of my allies if I were seen drinking your wines and eating your chicken."
10110{_}1923{_}"By the way, how did you know I had chickens in store, and a spit on which to roast them?"
10110{_}1924{_}"I looked you over at five-thirty this morning, having traveled from London by the mail train.
10110{_}1925{_}I must lecture you on your inefficient window-catches, Mr. Grant.
10110{_}1926{_}Several self-respecting burglars of my acquaintance would give your house the go-by as being too easy.
10110{_}1927{_}And, one other matter.
10110{_}1928{_}I suggest that any man who mentions the Steynholme murder again before the coffee arrives shall be fined a sovereign for each offense, such fine, or fines, to form a fund for the relief of his hearers.
10110{_}1929{_}_Cre nom d'un pipe_!
10110{_}1930{_}Three intelligent men can surely discuss more interesting topics while they eat!"
10110{_}1931{_}CHAPTER VIII  AN INTERRUPTED SYMPOSIUM   "Have a cigarette," said Grant to Furneaux, when the blinds were drawn, a lamp lighted, and the sherry dispensed.
10110{_}1932{_}"Thank you."
10110{_}1933{_}The self-invited guest took one.
10110{_}1934{_}He sniffed it, broke the paper wrapping, and crumbled some of the tobacco between finger and thumb.
10110{_}1935{_}"Ah, those Greeks!"
10110{_}1936{_}he said sadly.
10110{_}1937{_}"They simply can't go straight.
10110{_}1938{_}This brand of Turk used to be made of a tobacco grown on a slope above Salonica.
10110{_}1939{_}A strip of sun-baked soil built up a reputation which is now being bartered for filthy lucre by the use of Egyptian 'fillings.'"
10110{_}1940{_}"You're a connoisseur, Mr. Hawknose--try these," said Hart, proffering a case, from which the detective drew a cigarette, throwing the other one aside.
10110{_}1941{_}"Why 'Hawknose'?"
10110{_}1942{_}he inquired.
10110{_}1943{_}"A blend.
10110{_}1944{_}First syllable of Hawkshaw and second of Furneaux--the latter Anglicized, of course."
10110{_}1945{_}"And vulgarized."
10110{_}1946{_}"You prefer Furshaw, perhaps?"
10110{_}1947{_}"Either effort is feeble for a man who can write about South America, and be lucid.
10110{_}1948{_}Do you smoke this stuff, may I ask?"
10110{_}1949{_}While talking, he had smelt and destroyed the second cigarette.
10110{_}1950{_}"If it's a fair question, what the devil do _you_ smoke?"
10110{_}1951{_}cried Hart.
10110{_}1952{_}"Nothing.
10110{_}1953{_}I'm a non-smoker.
10110{_}1954{_}My profession demands a clear intellect, not a brain atrophied by nicotine."
10110{_}1955{_}"Piffle!
10110{_}1956{_}Carlyle and Bismarck were smokers."
10110{_}1957{_}"Who reads Carlyle now-a-days?
10110{_}1958{_}And what modern German pays heed to Bismarck's dogmas?
10110{_}1959{_}Look at that pipe of yours.
10110{_}1960{_}It was once a pure ivory white.
10110{_}1961{_}Now it is black--soiled by tobacco juice.
10110{_}1962{_}Your lungs are slowly emulating it, and your wits will cloud in time.
10110{_}1963{_}Read Tolstoi, Mr. Hart.
10110{_}1964{_}He will teach you how nicotine deadens the conscience."
10110{_}1965{_}"At last I know why I smoke like a Thames tug," laughed Hart, "but I'm blest if I can understand why _you_ make such a study of the vile weed."
10110{_}1966{_}"Most criminals are addicted to the habit.
10110{_}1967{_}I classify them by their brand of tobacco.
10110{_}1968{_}For instance, a clever forger would never descend to thick twist, while a swell mobsman would turn with horror from a woodbine."
10110{_}1969{_}Minnie entered, and nodded, whereupon Grant led the others upstairs to wash. From the bathroom he looked out over a darkening landscape.
10110{_}1970{_}Doris's dormer window was open.
10110{_}1971{_}She was leaning on the sill, but he could not tell whether or not her eyes were turned his way.
10110{_}1972{_}Her attitude was pensive, disconsolate, curiously forlorn for a girl normally high-spirited.
10110{_}1973{_}He was on the point of signaling to her when he remembered Furneaux's presence.
10110{_}1974{_}There was something impish, almost diabolically clever, in that little man's characteristics which induced wariness.
10110{_}1975{_}The dinner was a marvel, considering the short notice given to the cook.
10110{_}1976{_}Luckily, Mrs. Bates, a loyal soul, had resolved to tempt her employer's appetite that evening.
10110{_}1977{_}Village gossip had it that the police were about to arrest him, and she was determined he should enjoy at least one good meal before being haled to prison.
10110{_}1978{_}Hence, the materials were present.
10110{_}1979{_}The rest was a matter of quantities, and Sussex seldom stints itself in that respect.
10110{_}1980{_}The chatter round the table was light and amusing.
10110{_}1981{_}The three were well matched conversationally.
10110{_}1982{_}Furneaux evidently held the opinion once expressed by a notable Walrus--that the time had come  To talk of many things: Of shots--and ships--and sealing-wax-- Of cabbages--and kings.
10110{_}1983{_}He was in excellent form, and the others played up to him.
10110{_}1984{_}Hart's slow drawl was ever trenchant and witty, and Grant forgot his woes in congenial company.
10110{_}1985{_}As for the mercurial detective himself, it might be said of him as of the school-master of Auburn:  And still they gazed, and still the wonder grew, That one small head could carry all he knew.
10110{_}1986{_}It was he who dropped them with a bounce from the realm of fancy to the unpleasing region of ugly fact.
10110{_}1987{_}No sooner had Minnie cleared the table, and brought in the coffee, than he whisked around on Grant as though hitherto he had been only awaiting an opportunity of scarifying him.
10110{_}1988{_}"Now," he said, propping an elbow on the table, and supporting his chin on a clenched fist, "the embargo is off the Steynholme affair.
10110{_}1989{_}_You_ didn't kill Adelaide Melhuish, Mr. Grant.
10110{_}1990{_}Who did?"
10110{_}1991{_}"I wish I could tell you," was the emphatic answer.
10110{_}1992{_}"Do you suspect anybody?
10110{_}1993{_}You needn't fear the libel law in confiding your secret thought to me, and I assume that Mr. Hart is trustworthy--where his friends are concerned?"
10110{_}1994{_}"Why that unkind differentiating clause, my pocket Vidocq?"
10110{_}1995{_}put in Hart.
10110{_}1996{_}"Because two Kings and a baker's dozen of Presidents have, at various times, sent most unflattering reports to this country about you."
10110{_}1997{_}"I must have annoyed 'em most damnably."
10110{_}1998{_}"You had.
10110{_}1999{_}I congratulate you, but Heaven only knows where I may convoy you some day on an extradition warrant....Proceed, Mr.
10110{_}2000{_}Grant."
10110{_}2001{_}"I assure you, on my honor, that the only reasonable suggestion I can make is that put forward by my gardener to-day," said Grant.
10110{_}2002{_}"He thinks that the murder must have been committed by a lunatic.
10110{_}2003{_}I can offer no other hypothesis."
10110{_}2004{_}"Your gardener may be right.
10110{_}2005{_}But what lunatic, barring yourself and the horse-coper, Elkin, is in love with Doris Martin?"
10110{_}2006{_}Like Elkin the previous night, Grant struck the table till things rattled.
10110{_}2007{_}"Keep her name out of it," he cried fiercely.
10110{_}2008{_}"You are a man of the world, not a suspicious idiot of the Robinson type.
10110{_}2009{_}You heard to-day the full and true explanation of her presence here on Monday night.
10110{_}2010{_}It was a sheer accident.
10110{_}2011{_}Why harp on Doris Martin rather than any member of the Bates family?"
10110{_}2012{_}"Who, may I ask, is Doris Martin?"
10110{_}2013{_}put in Hart.
10110{_}2014{_}"The Steynholme postmaster's daughter," said Furneaux.
10110{_}2015{_}"A remarkably pretty and intelligent girl.
10110{_}2016{_}If her father was a peer she would be the belle of a London season.
10110{_}2017{_}As it is, her good looks seem to have put a maggot in more than one nut in this village."
10110{_}2018{_}Hart waved the negro's head in the air.
10110{_}2019{_}"The lunatic theory for mine," he declared.
10110{_}2020{_}"If one woman's lovely face could bring a thousand ships to Ilion, why should not another's drive men to madness in Steynholme?"
10110{_}2021{_}"Well phrased, sir," cackled Furneaux delightedly.
10110{_}2022{_}"I'll wangle that in on a respected colleague of mine, who is a whale at deducing a proposition from given premises, but cannot induce a general fact from particular instances to save his life ... Now, stifle your romantic frenzy, Mr. Grant, and listen to me.
10110{_}2023{_}If you were minded to instruct me in the art of writing good English, I would sit at your feet an attentive disciple.
10110{_}2024{_}When I, Furneaux, of the 'Yard,' lay down a first principle in the investigation of crime, I expect deference on your part.
10110{_}2025{_}I tell you unhesitatingly that if Doris Martin didn't exist, Adelaide Melhuish would be alive now.
10110{_}2026{_}That, as a thesis, is nearly as certain a thing as that the sun will rise to-morrow.
10110{_}2027{_}I go farther, and hazard the guess, not the fixed belief, though my guesses are usually borne out by events, that if Doris Martin had not been in this garden at half past ten on Monday night, Adelaide Melhuish would not have been killed some twenty minutes later.
10110{_}2028{_}It is useless for you to fume and rage in vain effort to disprove either of these presumptive facts.
10110{_}2029{_}You are simply beating the air.
10110{_}2030{_}This mystery centers in and around the postmaster's daughter.
10110{_}2031{_}Come, now, you are a reasonable person.
10110{_}2032{_}Admit the cold, hard truth, and then give play to your fancy."
10110{_}2033{_}"Sir," said Hart, brandishing his pipe again, "I suggest that you and I, here and now, form a mutual admiration society."
10110{_}2034{_}"It is a cruel and bitter thing that an innocent girl should be dragged into association with a foul crime," said Grant stubbornly.
10110{_}2035{_}"I am not disputing the force of your acumen, Mr. Furneaux.
10110{_}2036{_}My only desire is to shield the good name of a very charming young lady."
10110{_}2037{_}"What's done can't be undone," countered the detective, well knowing that Grant confessed himself beaten.
10110{_}2038{_}"But what is all the bother about?
10110{_}2039{_}You heard from Miss Martin's own lips absolutely the whole truth, and nothing but the truth.
10110{_}2040{_}Put her in the witness-box, and what more can she tell you?"
10110{_}2041{_}"I am not worrying about her appearance in the witness-box," said Furneaux dryly.
10110{_}2042{_}"Long before that stage is reached I shall be hunting a star burglar, or, perhaps, looking into the Foreign Office _dossier_ of our worthy friend here, as to-day's papers hint at trouble in Venezuela.
10110{_}2043{_}No, sir.
10110{_}2044{_}The county police will get all the credit.
10110{_}2045{_}P.C.
10110{_}2046{_}Robinson will be swanking about then, telling the yokels what _he_ did.
10110{_}2047{_}I, with Olympic nod, say, 'There's your man!'
10110{_}2048{_}and the handcuffs' brigade do the rest.
10110{_}2049{_}So far as I can foresee, Miss Martin's name may be spared any undue prominence in this inquiry.
10110{_}2050{_}I go even farther, and promise that anything I can do in that way shall be done."
10110{_}2051{_}"That is very kind and considerate of you," said Grant gratefully.
10110{_}2052{_}"Don't halloo till you're out of the wood."
10110{_}2053{_}said Furneaux, sitting back suddenly and nursing his left knee with clasped hands.
10110{_}2054{_}"I can't control other people's actions, you know.
10110{_}2055{_}What I insist on to-night is that you shall envisage this affair in its proper light.
10110{_}2056{_}We have a long way to travel before counsel rises with his smug 'May it please you, me lud, and gentlemen of the jury.'
10110{_}2057{_}But, having persuaded you to agree that, willy nilly, Miss Doris is the hub of our little universe for the hour, I now swear you and this fire-eater in as assistants.
10110{_}2058{_}There must be no more speeches, no punching of heads, very little love-making, and that by order--"  "Has the postmaster's daughter a delectable sister, O Liliputian cop?"
10110{_}2059{_}demanded Hart.
10110{_}2060{_}"No.
10110{_}2061{_}Two of 'em would have caused a riot long since.
10110{_}2062{_}Mr. Grant will do all, and more than all, necessary in that direction."
10110{_}2063{_}Grant leaned forward.
10110{_}2064{_}He spoke very earnestly.
10110{_}2065{_}"I want you to believe me when I tell you," he said, "that I never gave serious thought to the notion of marrying Miss Martin until such a possibility was suggested last night by that swab, Ingerman."
10110{_}2066{_}"Ah, Ingerman!
10110{_}2067{_}You kept a record of what he said, I gather?"
10110{_}2068{_}"Yes, here it is."
10110{_}2069{_}Grant rose, and went to a writing-desk with nests of drawers which stood against the wall on the left of the door.
10110{_}2070{_}He never used it for its primary purpose.
10110{_}2071{_}When the table was laid for meals, Minnie or her mother had orders to remove all papers and books to the top of the desk.
10110{_}2072{_}The house contained no other living-room of size.
10110{_}2073{_}The hall was spacious; a smoking den next the dining-room had degenerated into a receptacle of guns, fishing-rods, golf-clubs, Alpenstocks, skis and other such sporting accessories.
10110{_}2074{_}The remainder of the ground-floor accommodation was given up to the Bateses.
10110{_}2075{_}Unlocking a drawer, Grant produced a notebook, which he handed to Furneaux.
10110{_}2076{_}The detective laid it on the table.
10110{_}2077{_}He was sitting with his back to the large window.
10110{_}2078{_}Hart faced him.
10110{_}2079{_}Grant's chair was between the two.
10110{_}2080{_}"By the way, as you're on your feet, Mr. Grant," said Furneaux, "you might just show me exactly where you were standing when you saw the face at the window."
10110{_}2081{_}"For the love of Mike, what's this?"
10110{_}2082{_}gurgled Hart.
10110{_}2083{_}"'The face at the window'; 'the postmaster's daughter.'
10110{_}2084{_}How many more catchy cross-heads will you bring into the story?"
10110{_}2085{_}"Poor Adelaide Melhuish undoubtedly came here on Monday night and looked in at me while I was at work," said Grant sadly.
10110{_}2086{_}"You know the history of my calf love three years ago, Wally."
10110{_}2087{_}"Shall I ever forget it?
10110{_}2088{_}You bored me stiff about it.
10110{_}2089{_}Then, when the crash came, you walked me off my legs in the Upper Engadine.
10110{_}2090{_}Ugh!
10110{_}2091{_}That night on the Forno glacier.
10110{_}2092{_}It gives me a chill to think of it now.
10110{_}2093{_}Furneaux, pass the port.
10110{_}2094{_}Your name is wrongly spelt.
10110{_}2095{_}It should be fourneau, not Furneaux.
10110{_}2096{_}A little oven.
10110{_}2097{_}Hot stuff.
10110{_}2098{_}Got me?"
10110{_}2099{_}"My _dear_ Hart, you flatter me," retorted the detective instantly.
10110{_}2100{_}"How long am I to pose here?"
10110{_}2101{_}snapped Grant.
10110{_}2102{_}"Sorry," said Furneaux.
10110{_}2103{_}"These interruptions are banal.
10110{_}2104{_}Is that where you were?"
10110{_}2105{_}"Yes.
10110{_}2106{_}I had my hand outstretched for a book.
10110{_}2107{_}It's dark in this corner.
10110{_}2108{_}When I want to find a book I light a candle, which is always placed on the ledge of the window for the purpose.
10110{_}2109{_}The blind was not drawn that night.
10110{_}2110{_}It seldom is.
10110{_}2111{_}I had the book in my hand, and had found the required passage when I chanced to look at the window and saw _her_ face."
10110{_}2112{_}"Do you mind reconstructing the scene.
10110{_}2113{_}This lamp was on the table, I suppose?"
10110{_}2114{_}"Yes."
10110{_}2115{_}"Well, pull up the blind, light your candle, and find the book.
10110{_}2116{_}Act the whole incident, in fact."
10110{_}2117{_}Grant obeyed.
10110{_}2118{_}He held the candlestick until he had picked out the particular volume; then he placed it in the recess of the window, and searched through the pages of the book.
10110{_}2119{_}Furneaux bent forward so as to watch the rehearsal and catch the effect of the light externally.
10110{_}2120{_}The hour was not so late as when Adelaide Melhuish, or her ghost, gazed in through one of those narrow panes, but the night was dark enough to lend the necessary _vraisemblance_.
10110{_}2121{_}Hart, deeply interested, looked on with rapt, eager eyes.
10110{_}2122{_}For a full minute the tableau remained thus.
10110{_}2123{_}Then, with a rapidity born of many a close 'scape in wild lands, Hart drew a revolver from a hip pocket, and fired at the window.
10110{_}2124{_}He alone was in a position to see through all parts of it.
10110{_}2125{_}Grant was still thumbing a small brown volume in the manner of one who knew that a certain passage would be found therein but was ignorant of its exact place in the text.
10110{_}2126{_}Furneaux, intent on his every movement, had only a side-long view of the window, which, it will be remembered, formed a tiny rectangle in a thick wall.
10110{_}2127{_}The revolver was a heavy-caliber weapon, and the explosion blew out the lamp.
10110{_}2128{_}The flame of the candle flickered, owing either to the passage of the bullet or the disturbance of the air.
10110{_}2129{_}But it burnt steadily again within the fifth part of a second, and they all saw a starred hole in the center pane of glass of the second tier from the bottom.
10110{_}2130{_}"What fool's game are you playing?"
10110{_}2131{_}shrilled Furneaux, nevertheless active as a wildcat in his spring to the French window, there to snatch at the blind and turn the knob which controlled a lever bolt.
10110{_}2132{_}"Laying another ghost--one with whiskers," said Hart coolly.
10110{_}2133{_}"I got him, too, I think."
10110{_}2134{_}"You must be mad, mad!"
10110{_}2135{_}shrieked the detective, tearing open the window, and vanishing.
10110{_}2136{_}"For Heaven's sake, Wally, no more shooting!"
10110{_}2137{_}cried Grant, running after Furneaux.
10110{_}2138{_}Minnie and her mother appeared at the dining-room door.
10110{_}2139{_}Finding the place in semi-obscurity, and reeking with gunpowder, they screamed loudly.
10110{_}2140{_}"You Steynholme folk are all on the jump," said Hart.
10110{_}2141{_}"Cheer up, fair dames!
10110{_}2142{_}Thunder relieves the atmosphere, you know, and one live cartridge is often more effective than an ocean of talk."
10110{_}2143{_}"Bub-bub-but who's shot, sir?"
10110{_}2144{_}gasped Minnie.
10110{_}2145{_}"A ghost, a most scoundrelly apparition, with fearsome eyes, offensive whiskers, and a hat which is a base copy of mine."
10110{_}2146{_}"Owd Ben!"
10110{_}2147{_}sighed Mrs. Bates, collapsing straightway in a faint.
10110{_}2148{_}Luckily, Minnie caught her mother and broke her fall, because the housekeeper was large and solid, and might have been seriously injured otherwise.
10110{_}2149{_}Hart was distressed by this development, but, being eminently a ready person in an emergency, he rose to the occasion by extracting the empty case from the revolver, and holding it to the poor woman's nostrils, while supporting her with an arm and a knee.
10110{_}2150{_}"This is far more effective than burnt brown paper, Minnie," he said.
10110{_}2151{_}"Now, don't get excited, but mix some brandy and water, and we'll have your mother telling us who Owd Ben is, or was, before Hawk-eye comes back to disturb us.
10110{_}2152{_}Judging by the noises I hear, he's busy outside."
10110{_}2153{_}"That's father!"
10110{_}2154{_}shrieked Minnie hysterically.
10110{_}2155{_}"Good Lord!
10110{_}2156{_}Has your father--"  For an instant, Hart was nearly alarmed, but Grant's voice came authoritatively:  "It's all right, Bates.
10110{_}2157{_}Let go, I tell you!"
10110{_}2158{_}"Phew!"
10110{_}2159{_}said Hart.
10110{_}2160{_}"I was on the point of confusing your respected dad with Owd Ben ... That's it, ma!
10110{_}2161{_}Sniff hard!
10110{_}2162{_}As a cook you're worth your weight in gold, which is some cook."
10110{_}2163{_}Meanwhile, Furneaux, seeing that no dead body was stretched on the strip of grass beneath the window, dashed into the shrubbery to the right, and was clutched in a mighty embrace by an older but much more powerful man in Bates, who had hurried from the front of the house on hearing the pistol-shot.
10110{_}2164{_}Most fortunately, the gardener, deeming his vigil a needless one, had not armed himself with a stick, or the consequences might have been grave.
10110{_}2165{_}As it was, no one except Hart had been vouchsafed sight or sound of the latest specter, which, however, had left a very convincing souvenir of its visit in the shape of a soft felt hat with two bullet holes through the crown.
10110{_}2166{_}Furneaux, quivering with silent wrath, soon abandoned the search when this _piece de conviction_ was found at the root of the Dorothy Perkins rose-tree.
10110{_}2167{_}Seeing the lamp relighted, he peremptorily bade Grant and Bates come in with him.
10110{_}2168{_}He closed the window, adjusted the blind again, and poured generous measures of port wine into two glasses.
10110{_}2169{_}Handing one to Bates, he took the other himself.
10110{_}2170{_}"Friend," he said, "some men have fame thrust upon them, but you have achieved it.
10110{_}2171{_}To-night you pierced the heel of Achilles.
10110{_}2172{_}Here's to you!"
10110{_}2173{_}"I dunno wot 'ee's saying mister, but 'good health'," said Bates, swigging the wine with gusto.
10110{_}2174{_}"Now, for your master's sake, not a word to a soul about this hubbub."
10110{_}2175{_}"Right you are, sir!
10110{_}2176{_}But that there pryin' Robinson wur on t' bridge five minutes since.
10110{_}2177{_}And, by gum, here he is!"
10110{_}2178{_}A determined knock and ring came at the front door.
10110{_}2179{_}Minnie, helped by Hart, had just escorted Mrs. Bates to the kitchen.
10110{_}2180{_}"Let _me_ go!"
10110{_}2181{_}said Furneaux, darting out into the hall.
10110{_}2182{_}He opened the door, and thrust his face into the police-constable's, startling the latter considerably.
10110{_}2183{_}Before Robinson could utter a syllable, the detective hissed a question.
10110{_}2184{_}"Did anyone cross the bridge after that shot was fired?"
10110{_}2185{_}"Nun--No, sir," stuttered the other.
10110{_}2186{_}"You saw no one running along the road?"
10110{_}2187{_}"Saw nothing, sir."
10110{_}2188{_}"Very well.
10110{_}2189{_}Glad to find you're on the job.
10110{_}2190{_}Don't let on you met me here.
10110{_}2191{_}Good-night!"
10110{_}2192{_}Mighty is Scotland Yard with the provincial police.
10110{_}2193{_}Robinson was back on his self-imposed beat before he well realized that he knew neither why nor by whom nor by what sort of weapon the commotion had been created.
10110{_}2194{_}But he was quite sure the noise came from the garden front of Mr. Grant's house.
10110{_}2195{_}"That little hop-o'-me-thumb thinks he's smart, dam smart," he communed angrily, "but I've taken a line of me own, an' I'll stick to it, though the Yard sends down twenty men!"
10110{_}2196{_}He heard footsteps coming down a paved footpath which ran like a white riband through the cobble-beaded width of the high-street, and withdrew swiftly to the shelter of a disused tannery adjoining the village end of the bridge.
10110{_}2197{_}A cloaked female figure sped past.
10110{_}2198{_}Though the night was rather dark for June, he had no difficulty in recognizing Doris Martin's graceful movements.
10110{_}2199{_}No other girl in Steynholme walked like her.
10110{_}2200{_}She was slim enough to dispense with tight corsets, and tall enough to wear low-heeled shoes, nor did she need to pinch her toes in order to gain the semblance of small feet.
10110{_}2201{_}After her went Robinson, keyed to exultation by this outcome of his watchfulness.
10110{_}2202{_}She was going to The Hollies, of course.
10110{_}2203{_}The road led to Knoleworth, and no young woman of her age in the village would dream of taking a lonely walk in the country at ten o'clock at night.
10110{_}2204{_}For a man of his height and somewhat ponderous build, the policeman followed with real stealth.
10110{_}2205{_}Thus, when she turned in at the gate, he was there by the time she had reached the front door.
10110{_}2206{_}He heard her pull the bell.
10110{_}2207{_}Curiously enough, to his thinking, Furneaux again appeared.
10110{_}2208{_}"Is Mr. Grant at home?"
10110{_}2209{_}he heard Doris say.
10110{_}2210{_}"Yes.
10110{_}2211{_}Will you come in?"
10110{_}2212{_}replied the detective.
10110{_}2213{_}"Is he--is all well here?"
10110{_}2214{_}"Quite, I assure you.
10110{_}2215{_}But _do_ come in.
10110{_}2216{_}I'll escort you home.
10110{_}2217{_}I'm going to the inn in five minutes."
10110{_}2218{_}Doris, after hesitating a little, entered.
10110{_}2219{_}Robinson crept on tiptoe over a stretch of gravel, and took to the shrubbery.
10110{_}2220{_}It was high time, he thought, that the local constabulary learnt what was going on in that abode of mystery.
10110{_}2221{_}CHAPTER IX  HE WHOM THE CAP FITS--   Several minutes had elapsed between the two unexpected visits.
10110{_}2222{_}During those minutes a somewhat acrimonious discussion broke out in the dining-room.
10110{_}2223{_}Bates went to reassure his wife, and Hart sauntered back from the kitchen.
10110{_}2224{_}He was received by Furneaux and Grant more in sorrow than in anger, a pose on their part which he blandly disregarded.
10110{_}2225{_}He helped himself to the remains of the decanter of port.
10110{_}2226{_}"The next point of vital interest in the narrative is to establish, by such evidence as is available, who Owd Ben is, or was," he said.
10110{_}2227{_}"I presume, since he had attained local celebrity as a ghost, he has passed over, as the spiritists say."
10110{_}2228{_}"Sit down!"
10110{_}2229{_}cried Furneaux savagely.
10110{_}2230{_}Hart sat down, and began filling that portentous pipe.
10110{_}2231{_}"You fellows merely ran into each other outside, I take it," he said, apparently by way of a chatty remark.
10110{_}2232{_}"The crack of the pistol-shot and the supposed resurrection of Owd Ben threw Mrs. Bates temporarily off her balance, so I helped in reviving her.
10110{_}2233{_}Between such a cook and such a ghost, who would hesitate?"
10110{_}2234{_}When Furneaux was really irritated, he swore in French.

10110{_}2552{_}They're stored in the loft over the club-room--the room where the inquest wur held."
10110{_}2553{_}"What, _here_?"

10110{_}2568{_}CHAPTER X  THE CASE AGAINST GRANT   Next morning, after a long conference with Superintendent Fowler, from which, to his great chagrin, P. C. Robinson was excluded, Furneaux went to the post office, dispatched an apparently meaningless telegram to a code address, and exchanged a few orthodox remarks with Doris and her father about the continued fine weather.
10110{_}2569{_}While he was yet at the counter, Ingerman crossed the road and entered the chemist's shop.
10110{_}2570{_}"Let me see," said the detective musingly, "by committing a slight trespass on your left-hand neighbor's garden, can I reach the yard of the inn?"
10110{_}2571{_}"What the eye doesn't see the heart doesn't grieve over," smiled Doris.
10110{_}2572{_}"Mrs. Jefferson went to Knoleworth early to-day, and took her maid.
10110{_}2573{_}By shopping at the stores there, they save their fares, and have a day out each week."
10110{_}2574{_}"May I go that way, then?"
10110{_}2575{_}he said.
10110{_}2576{_}"Suppose you send that goggle-eyed skivvy of yours on an errand."
10110{_}2577{_}This was done, and Furneaux made the desired transit.
10110{_}2578{_}Now, Tomlin, to whom the comings and goings of all and sundry formed the staple of the day's gossip, had seen the detective go out, but could "take his sollum davy" that the queer little man had not returned.
10110{_}2579{_}He, too, had watched Ingerman going to Siddle's.
10110{_}2580{_}Ten minutes later Elkin came down the hill, and headed for the same rendezvous.
10110{_}2581{_}Five minutes more, and Hobbs, the butcher, joined the others.
10110{_}2582{_}Tomlin was seething with curiosity, but there were some casual customers in the "snug," so he could not abandon his post.
10110{_}2583{_}Soon, however, Ingerman led Elkin and Hobbs to the inn.
10110{_}2584{_}Evidently, the "financier" had been making some small purchases.
10110{_}2585{_}He was in high spirits.
10110{_}2586{_}Ordering appetizers before the mid-day meal, he announced that he was returning to London that afternoon, but would be in Steynholme again for the adjourned inquest.
10110{_}2587{_}"No matter how my business suffers, I mean to see this affair through," he vowed.
10110{_}2588{_}"You gentlemen can pretty well guess my private convictions.
10110{_}2589{_}You were good enough to give me your friendship, so I spoke as openly as one dares when no charge has actually been laid against any particular person."
10110{_}2590{_}"Ay," said Elkin, with whom sunshine seemed to disagree, because he looked miserably ill. "We know what you mean, Mr. Ingerman.

10110{_}2706{_}Neither at Knoleworth nor Victoria did Ingerman catch sight of the detective, though he was anxious either to make the journey in the company of the representative of Scotland Yard or arrange an early appointment with him.
10110{_}2707{_}True, he was not inclined to place the strange-mannered little man on the same high plane as that suggested by certain London journalists to whom he had spoken.
10110{_}2708{_}But he wanted to win the confidence of "the Yard" in connection with this case, and the belief that he was being avoided was nettling.
10110{_}2709{_}He found consolation, of a sort, in the illustrated papers.
10110{_}2710{_}One especially contained two pages of local pictures.
10110{_}2711{_}"Mr. Grant addressing the crowd," with full text, was very effective, while there were admirable studies of The Hollies and the "scene of the tragedy."
10110{_}2712{_}His own portrait was not flattering.
10110{_}2713{_}The sun had etched his Mephistophelian features rather sharply, whereas Grant looked a very fine fellow.
10110{_}2714{_}Ingerman would have been more than surprised were he privileged to overhear a conversation which began and ended before he reached his flat in North Kensington.
10110{_}2715{_}Furneaux, who had jumped into the fore part of the train at Knoleworth, and was out in a jiffy at Victoria, handed his bag to a station detective, and turned into Vauxhall Bridge Road, one of the quietest of London's main thoroughfares.
10110{_}2716{_}There he met a big man, dressed in tweeds, whose manifest concern at the moment seemed to center in a rather bad wrapping of a very good cigar.
10110{_}2717{_}"Ah!

10110{_}2722{_}"My own carelessness.

10110{_}2727{_}Like your cigar, this case has come unstuck."

10110{_}2735{_}Winter appeared to be devoting his mind to circumventing the vagaries of a fragile tobacco-leaf.

10110{_}2737{_}The press photographer described him accurately to Grant.

10110{_}2788{_}"Nothing extenuate, nor set down aught in malice," said Othello to Lodovico, and these Scotland Yard men, charged with so great a responsibility, never forgot the great-hearted Moor's advice.
10110{_}2789{_}When Winter took his seat in the train at five o'clock he could have drawn a plan of Steynholme, which he had never seen, and marked thereon the exact position of each house mentioned in this record.
10110{_}2790{_}Moreover, he was acquainted with the chief characters by sight, as it were.
10110{_}2791{_}And, finally, he and Furneaux had arranged a plan of campaign.
10110{_}2792{_}Furneaux refreshed a jaded intellect by an evening at the opera.

10110{_}2807{_}I'm a child in such matters, but, 'pon my honor, if tempted to pour out my hard-earned savings into the lap of a City magnate, I would disgorge here more readily than in some saloon-bar of finance, where the new mahogany glistens, and the typewriters click like machine-guns."
10110{_}2808{_}Ingerman was nettled.
10110{_}2809{_}He glanced at his correspondence.

10110{_}2819{_}"My mind was weary.
10110{_}2820{_}I wanted my wits about me when I tackled you."

10110{_}2825{_}"I shall even enjoy it.

10110{_}2829{_}"And the Aegean Transport Company, Limited?"
10110{_}2830{_}"Into which I was inveigled by Greeks.

10110{_}2832{_}"It's a sort of schooling.

10110{_}2845{_}I believe firmly that Grant was directly concerned in the murder.
10110{_}2846{_}And I shall justify my belief.
10110{_}2847{_}Within the past fortnight a _rapprochement_ between my wife and myself became possible.
10110{_}2848{_}It was spoken of, even reduced to the written word.
10110{_}2849{_}I have her letters.
10110{_}2850{_}Mine should be found among her belongings.

10110{_}2853{_}"Ah.

10110{_}2857{_}I think the theater was palling on her.
10110{_}2858{_}But I see now that she still cherished the dream of winning the man she loved--not me, her husband, but that handsome dilettante, Grant.
10110{_}2859{_}I take it, therefore, that she went to Steynholme to determine whether or not the glamour of the past was really dead.
10110{_}2860{_}Unfortunately, she witnessed certain idyllic passages between her one-time lover and a charming village girl.
10110{_}2861{_}Imagine the effect of this discovery on one of the artistic temperament.
10110{_}2862{_}'Hell hath no fury like a woman scorned,' and my unhappy wife would lash herself into an emotional frenzy.
10110{_}2863{_}She would tear a passion to rags.
10110{_}2864{_}Her very training on the stage would come to her aid in scathing words--perhaps threats.
10110{_}2865{_}If Grant remained cold to her appeal the village beauty should be made to suffer.
10110{_}2866{_}Then _he_ would flame into storm.
10110{_}2867{_}And so the upas-tree of tragedy spread its poisonous shade until reason fled, and some demon whispered, 'Kill!'
10110{_}2868{_}I find no flaw in my theory.
10110{_}2869{_}It explains the inexplicable.
10110{_}2870{_}Now, how does it strike you, Mr.
10110{_}2871{_}Furneaux?"

10110{_}2873{_}"Is that so?

10110{_}2920{_}"It shall be done."

10110{_}2923{_}But the "little Frenchman" was smiling, too.

10110{_}2926{_}Each of these drawbacks was a commendation to Furneaux.
10110{_}2927{_}In fact, the Steynholme mystery had taken quite a favorable turn during that talk with Ingerman.
10110{_}2928{_}CHAPTER XI  P. C. ROBINSON TAKES ANOTHER LINE   About the time Furneaux was whisked past The Hollies in Superintendent Fowler's dogcart, Grant and Hart were finishing luncheon, and planning a long walk to the sea.
10110{_}2929{_}Grant would dearly have liked to secure Doris's company, but good taste forbade that he should even invite her to share the ramble.
10110{_}2930{_}Thus, the death of a woman with whom he had not exchanged a word during three years had already set up a barrier between Doris and himself.
10110{_}2931{_}Though impalpable, it was effective.
10110{_}2932{_}It could neither be climbed nor avoided.
10110{_}2933{_}Quiet little Steynholme had suddenly become a rigid censor of morals and etiquette.
10110{_}2934{_}Until this evil thing was annihilated by slow process of law, Doris and he might meet only by chance and never remain long together.

10110{_}2942{_}"Well, that's so.
10110{_}2943{_}I forgot to ask the reason.
10110{_}2944{_}There was one, I suppose."
10110{_}2945{_}"Of the best.
10110{_}2946{_}That little man is a live wire of intelligence.
10110{_}2947{_}He's wasted on Scotland Yard.
10110{_}2948{_}He ought to be a dramatist or an ambassador."

10110{_}2950{_}"Not at all.
10110{_}2951{_}Each profession demands brains, and is at its best in coining cute phrases.

10110{_}2953{_}A bell rang.
