10110{_}3167{_}"What sort?
10110{_}3168{_}Racing, coaching, roadsters, or hacks?"
10110{_}3169{_}"All sorts.
10110{_}3170{_}The Argentine, where I have connections, offers an ever-open door to good horseflesh."
10110{_}3171{_}"Are you having a look round?"
10110{_}3172{_}"Yes.
10110{_}3173{_}There are several decent studs within driving distance of Steynholme.
10110{_}3174{_}Isn't that so, landlord?"
10110{_}3175{_}"Lots, sir," said Tomlin.
10110{_}3176{_}"An' the very man you're talkin' to has some stuff not to be sneezed at."
10110{_}3177{_}"Is that so?"
10110{_}3178{_}Mr. Franklin gazed at Elkin in a very friendly manner.
10110{_}3179{_}"May I ask your name, sir?"
10110{_}3180{_}Elkin produced a card.
10110{_}3181{_}Every hoof in his stables appreciated in value forthwith, but he was far too knowing that he should appear to rush matters.
10110{_}3182{_}"Call any day you like, sir," he said.
10110{_}3183{_}"Glad to see you.
10110{_}3184{_}But give me notice.
10110{_}3185{_}I generally have an appetizer here of a morning about eleven."
10110{_}3186{_}"An' you want it, too, Fred," said Hobbs.
10110{_}3187{_}"Dash me, you're as thin as a herrin'.
10110{_}3188{_}Stop whiskey an' drink beer, like me."
10110{_}3189{_}"And you might also follow that gentleman's example," interposed Siddle quietly, nodding towards Mr. Franklin.
10110{_}3190{_}"What's that?"
10110{_}3191{_}snapped Elkin.
10110{_}3192{_}"Don't worry about murders."
10110{_}3193{_}"That's a nice thing to say.
10110{_}3194{_}Why should _I_ worry about the d---d mix-up?"
10110{_}3195{_}The chemist made no reply, but Hobbs stepped into the breach valiantly.
10110{_}3196{_}"Keep yer 'air on, Fred," he vociferated.
10110{_}3197{_}"Siddle means no 'arm.
10110{_}3198{_}But wot else are yer a-doing of, mornin', noon, an' night?"
10110{_}3199{_}Elkin laughed, with his queer croak.
10110{_}3200{_}"If you stay here a day or two, you'll soon get to know what they're driving at, sir," he said to Franklin.
10110{_}3201{_}"The fact is that this chap, Grant, who found the body, and in whose garden the murder was committed, has been making eyes at the girl I'm as good as engaged to.
10110{_}3202{_}That would make anybody wild--now, wouldn't it?"
10110{_}3203{_}"Possibly," smiled Franklin.
10110{_}3204{_}"Of course there is always the lady's point of view.
10110{_}3205{_}The sex is proverbially fickle, you know.
10110{_}3206{_}'Woman, thy vows are traced in sand,' Lord Byron has it."
10110{_}3207{_}"Ay, an' some men's, too," guffawed Hobbs.
10110{_}3208{_}"Wot about Peggy Smith, Fred?"
10110{_}3209{_}Elkin blew a mouthful of cigarette smoke at the butcher.
10110{_}3210{_}"What about that tough old bull you bought at Knoleworth on Monday?"
10110{_}3211{_}he retorted.
10110{_}3212{_}Hobbs's face grew purple.
10110{_}3213{_}Mr. Franklin beckoned to Tomlin.
10110{_}3214{_}"Ask these gentlemen what they'll have," he said gently.
10110{_}3215{_}The landlord made a clatter of glasses, and the threatened storm passed.
10110{_}3216{_}"You've aroused my curiosity," remarked Franklin to Peters, but taking the company at large into the conversation.
10110{_}3217{_}"This does certainly strike one as a remarkable case.
10110{_}3218{_}Is there no suspicion yet as to the actual murderer?"
10110{_}3219{_}"None whatever," said Peters.
10110{_}3220{_}"That's what you may call the police opinion," broke in Elkin.
10110{_}3221{_}"We Steynholme folk have a pretty clear notion, I can assure you."
10110{_}3222{_}"The matter is still _sub judice_, and may remain so a long time," said Siddle.
10110{_}3223{_}"It is simply stupid to attach a kind of responsibility to the man who happens to occupy the house associated with the crime.
10110{_}3224{_}I have no patience with that sort of reasoning."
10110{_}3225{_}Hobbs, who did not want to quarrel with Elkin, suddenly championed him.
10110{_}3226{_}"That's all very well," he rumbled.
10110{_}3227{_}"But the hevidence you an' me 'eard, Siddle, an' the hevidence we know we're goin' to 'ear, is a lot stronger than that."
10110{_}3228{_}"I'm sure you'll pardon me, friends," said Siddle, rising with an apologetic smile, "but I happen to be foreman of the coroner's jury, and I feel that this matter is not for me, at any rate, to discuss publicly."
10110{_}3229{_}Out he went, not even heeding Tomlin's appeal to drink the ginger-ale he had just ordered.
10110{_}3230{_}"Just like 'im," sighed Hobbs.
10110{_}3231{_}"Good-'earted fellow!
10110{_}3232{_}Would find hexcuses for a black rat."
10110{_}3233{_}Elkin talked more freely now that the chemist's disapproving eye was off him.
10110{_}3234{_}Ultimately, Mr. Franklin elected to smoke a cigar in the open air, and strolled forth.
10110{_}3235{_}He sauntered down the hill, stood on the bridge, and admired the soft blue tones of the landscape in the half light of a summer evening.
10110{_}3236{_}Shortly before closing time, Robinson appeared, it being part of his routine duty to see that no noisy revelers disturbed the peace of the village.
10110{_}3237{_}He noticed the stranger at once, and elected to walk past him.
10110{_}3238{_}Thus, he received yet another shock when Mr. Franklin addressed him by name.
10110{_}3239{_}"Good evening, Robinson," said the pleasant, clear-toned voice.
10110{_}3240{_}"I've been expecting you to turn up.
10110{_}3241{_}Kindly go back home, and leave the door open.
10110{_}3242{_}I want to slip in quietly.
10110{_}3243{_}I am Chief Inspector Winter, of Scotland Yard."
10110{_}3244{_}"You don't say so, sir!"
10110{_}3245{_}stammered Robinson.
10110{_}3246{_}"But I do say it, and will prove it to you, of course.
10110{_}3247{_}I'll be with you in a minute or two.
10110{_}3248{_}There's someone coming.
10110{_}3249{_}You and I must not be seen together."
10110{_}3250{_}Robinson made off, and Winter lounged along the Knoleworth road.
10110{_}3251{_}He met Bates, going to the post with letters.
10110{_}3252{_}Naturally, Bates looked him over.
10110{_}3253{_}Returning from the post office, he kept a sharp eye for the unknown loiterer, but saw him not.
10110{_}3254{_}He even walked quickly to the bend of the road, but the other man had vanished.
10110{_}3255{_}Grant and Hart were talking of anything but the murder when Bates thrust his head in.
10110{_}3256{_}He was grasping his goatee beard, sure sign of some weight on his mind.
10110{_}3257{_}"Beg pardon," he said, "but I thought you'd like to know.
10110{_}3258{_}The place is just swarmin' with 'em."
10110{_}3259{_}"Bees?"
10110{_}3260{_}inquired Hart.
10110{_}3261{_}Bates stared fixedly at the speaker for a second or two.
10110{_}3262{_}"No, sir, 'tecs," he said.
10110{_}3263{_}"There's a big 'un now--just the opposite to the little 'un, Hawkshaw.
10110{_}3264{_}I 'ope I 'aven't to tackle this customer, though.
10110{_}3265{_}He'd gimme a doin', by the looks of 'im."
10110{_}3266{_}Bates had disappeared before Grant remembered that the press photographer had mentioned the Big 'Un and the Little 'Un of the Yard.
10110{_}3267{_}"Now, I wonder," he said.
10110{_}3268{_}His wonder could hardly have equaled Winter's had he heard the gardener's words.
10110{_}3269{_}The guess was a distinct score for blunt Sussex, though it was founded solely on the assumption that all comers now, unless Bates was personally acquainted with them, were limbs of the law.
10110{_}3270{_}CHAPTER XII  WHEREIN WINTER GETS TO WORK   Winter had identified Bates at the first glance.
10110{_}3271{_}The letters in the man's hand, too, showed his errand, so, while the gardener was climbing the hill, the detective slipped into Robinson's cottage.
10110{_}3272{_}He found the policeman awaiting him in the dark, because a voice said:  "Beg pardon, sir, but the other gentleman from the 'Yard' asked me to take him into the kitchen.
10110{_}3273{_}A light in the front room might attract attention, he thought."
10110{_}3274{_}"Just what Mr. Furneaux would suggest, and I agree with him," said Winter, quite alive to the canny discretion behind those words, "the other gentleman."
10110{_}3275{_}Robinson led the way.
10110{_}3276{_}Supper was laid on the table.
10110{_}3277{_}Poor Mrs. Robinson had again beaten a hasty retreat.
10110{_}3278{_}"Now, Robinson," said the Chief Inspector affably, "before we come to business I'll prove my bona fides.
10110{_}3279{_}Here is my official card, and I'll run quickly through events until 1.30 p.m. to-day.
10110{_}3280{_}I met Mr. Furneaux at Victoria, and he posted me fully up to that hour."
10110{_}3281{_}So the policeman listened to a clear summary of the Steynholme case as it was known to the authorities.
10110{_}3282{_}"I did not warn either Mr. Fowler or you of my visit because a telegram could hardly be explicit enough," concluded Winter.
10110{_}3283{_}"At the inn I am Mr. Franklin, an Argentine importer of blood stock in the horse line.
10110{_}3284{_}At this moment the only other man beside yourself in Steynholme who is aware of my official position is Mr. Peters, and he is pledged to secrecy.
10110{_}3285{_}To-morrow or any other day until further notice, you and I meet as strangers in public.
10110{_}3286{_}By the way, Mr. Furneaux asked me to tell you that he found the wig and the false beard in the river early this morning.
10110{_}3287{_}The wearer had apparently flung them off while crossing the foot-bridge leading from Bush Walk, having forgotten that they would not sink readily.
10110{_}3288{_}Perhaps he didn't care.
10110{_}3289{_}At any rate, Mr. Hart's bullet seems to have laid Owd Ben's ghost.
10110{_}3290{_}Now, what of this fellow, Elkin?
10110{_}3291{_}He worries me."
10110{_}3292{_}"Can I offer you a glass of beer, sir?"
10110{_}3293{_}"With pleasure.
10110{_}3294{_}May I smoke while you eat?
10110{_}3295{_}You see, I differ from Mr. Furneaux in both size and habits."
10110{_}3296{_}Robinson poured out the beer.
10110{_}3297{_}He was preternaturally grave.
10110{_}3298{_}The somewhat incriminating statements he had wormed out of the horse-dealer that afternoon lay heavy upon him.
10110{_}3299{_}But he told his story succinctly enough.
10110{_}3300{_}Winter nodded to emphasize each point, and congratulated him at the end.
10110{_}3301{_}"You arranged that very well," he said.
10110{_}3302{_}"I gather, though, that Elkin spoke rather openly."
10110{_}3303{_}"Just as I've put it, sir.
10110{_}3304{_}He tripped a bit over the time on Monday night.
10110{_}3305{_}But it's only fair to say that he might have had Tomlin's license in mind."
10110{_}3306{_}"That issue will be settled to-morrow.
10110{_}3307{_}I'll find out the commercial traveler's name, and send a telegram from Knoleworth before noon.... Who is Peggy Smith?"
10110{_}3308{_}Robinson set down an empty glass with a stare of surprise.
10110{_}3309{_}"Bob Smith's daughter, sir," he answered.
10110{_}3310{_}"No doubt.
10110{_}3311{_}But, proceed."
10110{_}3312{_}"Well, sir, she's just a village girl.
10110{_}3313{_}Her father is a blacksmith.
10110{_}3314{_}His forge is along to the right, not far.
10110{_}3315{_}She'll be twenty, or thereabouts."
10110{_}3316{_}"Frivolous?"
10110{_}3317{_}"Not more than the rest of 'em, sir."
10110{_}3318{_}"Have you seen her flirting with Elkin?"
10110{_}3319{_}Robinson took thought.
10110{_}3320{_}"Now that I come to think of it, she might be given a bit that way.
10110{_}3321{_}Her father shoes Elkin's nags, so there's a lot of comin' an' goin' between the two places.
10110{_}3322{_}But folks would always look on it as natural enough.
10110{_}3323{_}Yes, I've seen 'em together more than once."
10110{_}3324{_}"In that case, he can hardly grumble if the postmaster's daughter has an eye for another young man."
10110{_}3325{_}"Miss Martin!"
10110{_}3326{_}snorted Robinson.
10110{_}3327{_}"She wouldn't look the side of the road he was on.
10110{_}3328{_}Fred Elkin isn't her sort."
10110{_}3329{_}"But he said to-night in the Hare and Hounds that he and Miss Martin were practically engaged."
10110{_}3330{_}"Stuff an' nonsense!
10110{_}3331{_}Sorry, sir, but I admire Doris Martin.
10110{_}3332{_}I like to see a girl like her liftin' herself out of the common gang.
10110{_}3333{_}She's the smartest young lady in the village, an' not an atom of a snob.
10110{_}3334{_}No, no.
10110{_}3335{_}She isn't for Fred Elkin.
10110{_}3336{_}Before this murder cropped up everybody would have it that Mr. Grant would marry her."
10110{_}3337{_}"How does the murder intervene?"
10110{_}3338{_}Robinson shifted uneasily in his chair.
10110{_}3339{_}He knew only too well that he himself had driven a wedge between the two.
10110{_}3340{_}"Steynholme's a funny spot, sir," he contrived to explain.
10110{_}3341{_}"Since it came out that Doris an' Mr. Grant were in the garden at The Hollies at half past ten on Monday night, without Mr. Martin knowin' where his daughter was, there's been talk.
10110{_}3342{_}Both the postmaster an' the girl herself are up to it.
10110{_}3343{_}You can see it in their faces.
10110{_}3344{_}They don't like it, an' who can blame 'em!"
10110{_}3345{_}"Who, indeed?
10110{_}3346{_}But this Elkin--surely he had some ground for a definite boast, made openly, among people acquainted with all the parties?"
10110{_}3347{_}"There's more than Elkin would marry Doris if she lifted a finger, sir."
10110{_}3348{_}"Can you name them?"
10110{_}3349{_}"Well, Tomlin wants a wife."
10110{_}3350{_}Winter laughed joyously.
10110{_}3351{_}"Next?"
10110{_}3352{_}he cried.
10110{_}3353{_}"They say that Mr. Siddle is a widower."
10110{_}3354{_}"The chemist?
10110{_}3355{_}Foreman of the jury?"
10110{_}3356{_}"Yes, sir."
10110{_}3357{_}"From appearances, he is a likelier candidate than either Elkin or Tomlin.
10110{_}3358{_}Anybody else?"
10110{_}3359{_}"I shouldn't be far wrong if I gave you the name of most among the young unmarried men in the parish."
10110{_}3360{_}"Dear me!
10110{_}3361{_}I must have a peep at this charmer.
10110{_}3362{_}But I want those names, Robinson."
10110{_}3363{_}Winter produced a note-book, so he was evidently taking the matter seriously.
10110{_}3364{_}The policeman, however, was flustered.
10110{_}3365{_}His thoughts ran on Elkin, whereas this masterful person from London insisted on discussing Doris Martin.
10110{_}3366{_}"My difficulty is, sir, that she has never kep' company with any of 'em," he said.
10110{_}3367{_}"Never mind.
10110{_}3368{_}Give me the name of every man who, no matter what his position or prospects, might be irritated, if no more, if he knew that Miss Martin and Mr. Grant were presumably spooning in a garden at a rather late hour."
10110{_}3369{_}It was a totally new line of inquiry for Robinson, but he bent his wits to it, and evolved a list which, if published, would certainly be regarded with incredulous envy by every other girl in the village than the postmaster's daughter; as for Doris herself, she would be mightily surprised when she saw it, but whether annoyed or secretly gratified none but a pretty girl of nineteen can tell.
10110{_}3370{_}Winter departed soon afterwards.
10110{_}3371{_}Before going to the inn he had a look at the forge.
10110{_}3372{_}A young woman, standing at the open door of the adjoining cottage, favored him with a frank stare.
10110{_}3373{_}There was no light in the dwelling.
10110{_}3374{_}When he returned, after walking a little way down the road, the door was closed.
10110{_}3375{_}Next morning, Bates heard of Peters as the detective and of Mr. Franklin as a "millionaire" from South America.
10110{_}3376{_}Moreover, he scrutinized both in the flesh, and saw Robinson salute Peters but pass the financial potentate with indifference.
10110{_}3377{_}Alas, that a reputation, once built, should be destroyed!
10110{_}3378{_}"I was mistook, sir," he reported to Grant later.
10110{_}3379{_}"There's another 'tec about, but 'e ain't the chap I met last night.
10110{_}3380{_}They say this other bloke is rollin' in money, an' buyin' hosses right an' left."
10110{_}3381{_}"Then he'll soon be rolling in the mud, and have no money," put in Hart.
10110{_}3382{_}"Who is he?"
10110{_}3383{_}inquired Grant carelessly.
10110{_}3384{_}"A Mr. Franklin, from South America, sir."
10110{_}3385{_}Grant and Hart exchanged glances.
10110{_}3386{_}Curiously enough, Hart remained silent till Bates had gone.
10110{_}3387{_}"I must look this joker up, Jack," he said then.
10110{_}3388{_}"To me the mere mention of South America is like Mother Gary's chickens to a sailor, a harbinger of storm."
10110{_}3389{_}But Hart consumed Tomlin's best brew to no purpose--in so far as seeing Mr. Franklin was concerned, since the latter was in Knoleworth, buying a famous racing stud.
10110{_}3390{_}Being in the village, however, this fisher in troubled waters was not inclined to return without a bag of some sort.
10110{_}3391{_}He walked straight into the post office.
10110{_}3392{_}Doris and her father were there, the telegraphist being out.
10110{_}3393{_}"Good day, everybody," he cried cheerfully.
10110{_}3394{_}"Grant wants to know, Mr. Martin, if you and Miss Doris will come and dine with him, us, this evening at 7.30?"
10110{_}3395{_}The postmaster gazed helplessly at this free-and-easy stranger.
10110{_}3396{_}Doris laughed, and blushed a little.
10110{_}3397{_}"This is Mr. Hart, a friend of Mr. Grant's, dad," she explained.
10110{_}3398{_}"I'm afraid we cannot accept the invitation.
10110{_}3399{_}We are so busy."
10110{_}3400{_}"The worst of excuses," said Hart.
10110{_}3401{_}"But there is a London correspondent here who hands in a long telegram at that hour."
10110{_}3402{_}"What's his name?"
10110{_}3403{_}"Mr.
10110{_}3404{_}Peters."
10110{_}3405{_}"Great Scott!
10110{_}3406{_}Jimmie Peters here?
10110{_}3407{_}I'll soon put a stopper on him.
10110{_}3408{_}He'll come, too--jumping.
10110{_}3409{_}See if he doesn't.
10110{_}3410{_}Is it a bargain?
10110{_}3411{_}Short telegram at six.
10110{_}3412{_}Dinner for five at 7.30.
10110{_}3413{_}Come, now, Mr. Martin.
10110{_}3414{_}It's up to you.
10110{_}3415{_}I can see 'Yes' in Doris's eye.
10110{_}3416{_}Over the port--most delectable, I assure you--I'll give full details of the peculiar case of a man in Worcestershire whose crop of gooseberries increased fourfold after starting an apiary.
10110{_}3417{_}And what does it matter if you do lose a queen or two in June?
10110{_}3418{_}The drones will attend to that trifle....
10110{_}3419{_}It's a fixture, eh?
10110{_}3420{_}Where's Peters?
10110{_}3421{_}In the Pull and Push?
10110{_}3422{_}I'll rout him out."
10110{_}3423{_}The whirlwind subsided, but quickly materialized again.
10110{_}3424{_}"Peters nearly fell on his knees and wept with joy," announced Hart.
10110{_}3425{_}"He believes he was given a bull steak for luncheon.
10110{_}3426{_}He pledges himself to have only five hundred words on the wire at five o'clock."
10110{_}3427{_}Meanwhile, father and daughter had decided that there was no valid reason why they should not dine with Mr. Grant.
10110{_}3428{_}Martin already regretted his aloofness on the day of the inquest, though, truth to tell, Hart's expert knowledge of bee-culture was the determining factor.
10110{_}3429{_}On her part, Doris was delighted.
10110{_}3430{_}Her world had gone awry that week, and this small festivity might right it.
10110{_}3431{_}Not one word of the improvised dinner-party did Hart confide to Grant.
10110{_}3432{_}He informed the only indispensable person, Mrs. Bates, and left it at that.
10110{_}3433{_}Grant, a restless being these days, took him for another long walk.
10110{_}3434{_}It chanced that their road home led down the high-street.
10110{_}3435{_}The hour was a quarter past seven, and Peters hailed them.
10110{_}3436{_}Hart introduced the journalist, saying casually:  "Jimmie is coming to dinner, Jack."
10110{_}3437{_}"Delighted," said Grant, of course.
10110{_}3438{_}Peters looked slightly surprised, but passed no comment.
10110{_}3439{_}Then Doris and her father appeared.
10110{_}3440{_}They joined the others, shook hands, and, to Grant's secret perplexity, the whole party moved off down the hill in company.
10110{_}3441{_}When the Martins turned with the rest to cross the bridge, Grant began to suspect his friend.
10110{_}3442{_}"Wally," he managed to whisper, "what game have you been playing?"
10110{_}3443{_}"Aren't you satisfied?"
10110{_}3444{_}murmured Hart.
10110{_}3445{_}"Sdeath, as they used to say in the Surrey Theater, you're as bad as Furshaw!"
10110{_}3446{_}There were others far more perturbed by that odd conjunction of diners than the puzzled host, who merely expected Mrs. Bates to belabor him with a rolling pin.
10110{_}3447{_}Mr. Siddle, for instance, had just closed his shop when the five met.
10110{_}3448{_}That is to say, the dark blue blind was drawn, but the door was ajar.
10110{_}3449{_}He came to the threshold, and watched the party until the bridge was neared, when one of them, looking back, might have seen him, so he stepped discreetly inside.
10110{_}3450{_}Being a non-interfering, self-contained man, he seemed to be rather irresolute.
10110{_}3451{_}But that condition passed quickly.
10110{_}3452{_}Leaning over the counter, he secured a hat and a pair of field-glasses, and went out.
10110{_}3453{_}He, too, knew of Mrs. Jefferson's weakness for shopping in Knoleworth, and that good lady had gone there again.
10110{_}3454{_}Her train was due in ten minutes.
10110{_}3455{_}A wicket gate led to a narrow passage communicating with the back door of her residence.
10110{_}3456{_}He entered boldly, reached the garden, and hurried to the angle on the edge of the cliff next to the Martins' strip of ground.
10110{_}3457{_}Yes, a spacious dinner-table was laid at The Hollies.
10110{_}3458{_}Doris, Mr. Martin, and Peters soon strolled out on to the lawn.
10110{_}3459{_}The pedestrians had obviously gone upstairs to wash after their tramp.
10110{_}3460{_}Mr. Siddle rather forgot himself.
10110{_}3461{_}He stared so long and earnestly through the field-glasses that he ran full tilt into Mrs. Jefferson and maid before regaining the high-street.
10110{_}3462{_}But the chemist was a ready man.
10110{_}3463{_}He lifted his hat with an inquiring smile.
10110{_}3464{_}"Didn't you say you wanted some anti-arthritic salts early in the week?"
10110{_}3465{_}he asked.
10110{_}3466{_}"Yes," said Mrs. Jefferson, "but I got some to-day in Knoleworth, thank you."
10110{_}3467{_}"Well, I was just making up an indent, and might as well include your specific if you really needed it."
10110{_}3468{_}Which was kind and thoughtful of Mr. Siddle, but not quite true, though it fully explained his presence at Mrs. Jefferson's gate.
10110{_}3469{_}Mr. Franklin, escorting a fragrant Havana up the hill (he had traveled by the same train) saw the meeting, and, being aware of Mrs. Jefferson's frugal habits, since Furneaux had omitted no item of his movements in Steynholme, remembered it later during the nightly gathering in the inn.
10110{_}3470{_}Elkin greeted Mr. Franklin respectfully when the great man joined the circle.
10110{_}3471{_}"Did you see anything worth while at Knoleworth, sir?"
10110{_}3472{_}he said.
10110{_}3473{_}"No.
10110{_}3474{_}I was unlucky.
10110{_}3475{_}All the principals were at a race meeting."
10110{_}3476{_}"By gum!
10110{_}3477{_}That's right.
10110{_}3478{_}It's Gatwick today.
10110{_}3479{_}Dash!
10110{_}3480{_}I might have saved you a journey."
10110{_}3481{_}"Oh, it doesn't matter.
10110{_}3482{_}In my business there is no call for hurry."
10110{_}3483{_}Elkin looked around.
10110{_}3484{_}"Where's our friend, the 'tec?"
10110{_}3485{_}he said.
10110{_}3486{_}"I think you're wrong about 'im, meanin' Mr. Peters," said Tomlin.
10110{_}3487{_}"'E's 'ere for a noospaper, not for the Yard."
10110{_}3488{_}"That's his blarney," smirked Elkin.
10110{_}3489{_}"A detective doesn't go about telling everybody what he is."
10110{_}3490{_}"Whatever his profession may be," put in Siddle's quiet voice, "I happen to know that he is dining with Mr. Grant.
10110{_}3491{_}So are Mr. Martin and Doris.
10110{_}3492{_}By mere chance I called at Mrs. Jefferson's.
10110{_}3493{_}I went to the back door, and, finding it closed, looked into the garden.
10110{_}3494{_}From there I couldn't help seeing the assembly on the lawn of The Hollies."
10110{_}3495{_}"Dining at Grant's?"
10110{_}3496{_}shouted Elkin in a fury.
10110{_}3497{_}"Well, I'm--"  "'Ush, Fred!"
10110{_}3498{_}expostulated Tomlin with a shocked glance at Mr. Franklin.
10110{_}3499{_}"Wot's wrong wi' a bit of grub, ony ways?
10110{_}3500{_}A very nice-spoken young gent kem 'ere twiced, an' axed for Mr. Peters the second time.
10110{_}3501{_}He's a friend o' Mr. Grant's, I reckon."
10110{_}3502{_}"What's wrong?"
10110{_}3503{_}stormed the horse-dealer.
10110{_}3504{_}"Why, everything's wrong!
10110{_}3505{_}The bounder ought to be in jail instead of giving dinner-parties.
10110{_}3506{_}Imagine Doris eating in that house!"
10110{_}3507{_}"Ay!
10110{_}3508{_}Sweetbreads an' saddle o' lamb," interjected Hobbs with the air of one imparting a secret.
10110{_}3509{_}Elkin was pallid with wrath.
10110{_}3510{_}He glared at Hobbs.
10110{_}3511{_}"What I had in my mind was the impudence of the blighter," he said shrilly.
10110{_}3512{_}"That poor woman's body leaves here to-morrow for some cemetery in London, and Grant invites folk to a small dinner to-night!"
10110{_}3513{_}A sort of awe fell on the company.
10110{_}3514{_}None of the others had as yet put the two events in juxtaposition, and they had an ugly sound.
10110{_}3515{_}Even Mr. Siddle stifled a protest.
10110{_}3516{_}Elkin had scored a hit, a palpable hit, and no one could gainsay him.
10110{_}3517{_}He felt that, for once, the general opinion was with him, and drove the point home.
10110{_}3518{_}"Hobson--the local joiner and undertaker"--he explained for Mr. Franklin's benefit--"came this morning to borrow a couple of horses for the job.
10110{_}3519{_}It's to be done in style--'no expense spared' was Mr. Ingerman's order--and the poor thing is in her coffin now while Grant--"  He stopped.
10110{_}3520{_}Mr. Siddle coughed.
10110{_}3521{_}"You've said enough, Elkin," murmured the chemist.
10110{_}3522{_}"This excitement is harmful.
10110{_}3523{_}You really ought to be in bed for the next forty-eight hours, dieting yourself carefully, and taking Dr. Foxton's mixture regularly.
10110{_}3524{_}He has changed it, I noticed."
10110{_}3525{_}"Bed!
10110{_}3526{_}Me!
10110{_}3527{_}Not likely.
10110{_}3528{_}I'm going to kick up a row.
10110{_}3529{_}What are the police doing?
10110{_}3530{_}A set of blooming old women, that's what they are.
10110{_}3531{_}But I'll stir 'em up, if I have to write to the Home Secretary."
10110{_}3532{_}"Gentlemen," said Mr. Franklin, smiling genially, "I cannot help taking a certain interest in this affair.
10110{_}3533{_}May I, then, as a complete stranger to all concerned, tell you how this minor episode strikes me.
10110{_}3534{_}Mr. Grant, I understand, denies having seen or spoken to Miss Melhuish during the past three years.
10110{_}3535{_}None of the others now in his house had met her at all.
10110{_}3536{_}Really, if a man may not give a dinnerparty in these conditions, dining-out would become a lost art."
10110{_}3537{_}Elkin was obviously seeking for some retort which, though forcible, would not offend a possible patron.
10110{_}3538{_}But Siddle answered far more deftly than might be looked for from the horse-dealer.
10110{_}3539{_}"Your contention, sir, is just what the man of the world would hold," he said, "but, in this village, where we live on neighborly terms, such an incident would be impossible in almost any other house than The Hollies."
10110{_}3540{_}Mr. Franklin nodded.
10110{_}3541{_}He was convinced.
10110{_}3542{_}Tomlin, Hobbs, and a local draper bore out the chemist's reasonable theory.
10110{_}3543{_}Next morning Steynholme was again united in condemning Grant, while the postmaster and his daughter were not wholly exempted from criticism.
10110{_}3544{_}The dinner itself was an altogether harmless and cheery meal.
10110{_}3545{_}By common consent not one word was said about the murder.
10110{_}3546{_}Hart was amusing on the question of bees--almost flippant, Mr. Martin deemed him.
10110{_}3547{_}Peters had a wide store of strange experiences to draw on, while Grant, if rather silent in deference to two such brilliant talkers, found much satisfaction in regarding Doris as a hostess.
10110{_}3548{_}The next day being Saturday, or market day, the village was busy.
10110{_}3549{_}At eleven o'clock there was a somewhat unnecessary display of nodding plumes and long-tailed black horses at the removal of the coffin to the railway station.
10110{_}3550{_}For some reason, the funeral arrangements had not been bruited about until Elkin made that envenomed attack on Grant in the Hare and Hounds the previous night.
10110{_}3551{_}Ingerman had sent a gorgeous wreath, the only one forthcoming locally.
10110{_}3552{_}This fact, of course, invited comment, though no whisperer in the crowd troubled to add that the interment was only announced in that day's newspapers.
10110{_}3553{_}Peters, meeting Mr. Franklin on the stairs of the inn, put a note into his hand.
10110{_}3554{_}It read:  "Why don't you have a chat with Grant?
10110{_}3555{_}The public mind is being inflamed against him.
10110{_}3556{_}It's hardly fair."
10110{_}3557{_}Mr. Franklin, meeting Peters in the passage, winked at him, and the journalist tortured his brains to turn out some readable stuff which should grip the million on Sunday yet not to be damaging to the man whose hospitality he enjoyed over night.
10110{_}3558{_}In a word, the passing of Adelaide Melhuish was exploited thoroughly as an indictment of her one-time lover, and the only two in Steynholme not aware of the fact were Grant, himself, and Wally Hart.
10110{_}3559{_}By a singular coincidence, not ridiculously beyond the ken of a verger, when Doris went to church on Sunday morning, she found herself beside Mr. Franklin.
10110{_}3560{_}At the close of the service the same big man whom she had noticed as a neighbor in the pew overtook her at the post office door.
10110{_}3561{_}He lifted his hat.
10110{_}3562{_}A passer-by heard him say distinctly:  "Pardon me for troubling you, but can you tell me at what time the mail closes for London?"
10110{_}3563{_}"At four-thirty," said Doris.
10110{_}3564{_}No other person overheard Mr. Franklin's next words:  "I am now going to drop a letter in the box.
10110{_}3565{_}It's for you.
10110{_}3566{_}Get it at once.
10110{_}3567{_}It is of the utmost importance."
10110{_}3568{_}Doris was startled, as well she might be.
10110{_}3569{_}But--she went straight for the letter.
10110{_}3570{_}It was marked: "Private and Urgent," and ran:  DEAR MISS MARTIN.
10110{_}3571{_}I am here _vice_ Mr. Furneaux, who is engaged on other phases of the same inquiry.
10110{_}3572{_}My business is absolutely unknown.
10110{_}3573{_}I figure at the inn as "Mr. W. Franklin, Argentina."
10110{_}3574{_}Indeed, Mr. Furneaux left the village because he realized the difficulties facing him in that respect.
10110{_}3575{_}Now, I trust you, and I hope you will justify my faith.
10110{_}3576{_}You know Superintendent Fowler.
10110{_}3577{_}I want you to meet me and him this afternoon at two o'clock at the crossroads beyond the mill.
10110{_}3578{_}A closed car will be in waiting, and we can have half an hour's talk without anyone in Steynholme being the wiser.
10110{_}3579{_}Remember that this village, like the night, has a thousand eyes.
10110{_}3580{_}Naturally, I would not trouble you in this way if the cause was not vital to the ends of justice.
10110{_}3581{_}Whether or not you decide to keep this appointment, I have every confidence that you will respect my wish that _no one_, other than yourself, shall be informed of my identity.
10110{_}3582{_}But I believe you will be wise, and come.
10110{_}3583{_}I am,  Yours faithfully,  J.L.
10110{_}3584{_}WINTER,  Chief Inspector, C.I.D., Scotland Yard, S.W.
10110{_}3585{_}A card was inclosed, as a sort of credential.
10110{_}3586{_}But, somehow, it was not needed.
10110{_}3587{_}Doris had seen "Mr. Franklin" more than once, and she had heard him singing the hymns in church.
10110{_}3588{_}He looked worthy of credence.
10110{_}3589{_}His written words had the same honest ring.
10110{_}3590{_}She resolved to go.
10110{_}3591{_}Her father, sad to relate, had found three dead queens in the hives.
10110{_}3592{_}He was busy, but spared a moment to tell her that Mr. Siddle was coming to tea at four o'clock.
10110{_}3593{_}Doris was rather in a whirl, and seemed to be unnecessarily astonished.
10110{_}3594{_}"Mr. Siddle!
10110{_}3595{_}Why?"
10110{_}3596{_}she gasped.
10110{_}3597{_}"Why not!"
10110{_}3598{_}said her father.
10110{_}3599{_}"It's not the first time.
10110{_}3600{_}You can entertain him.
10110{_}3601{_}I'll look after the letters."
10110{_}3602{_}"I must get some cakes.
10110{_}3603{_}We have none."
10110{_}3604{_}"Well, that's simple.
10110{_}3605{_}I wonder if that fellow Hart really understands apiaculture?
10110{_}3606{_}You might invite him, too."
10110{_}3607{_}With that letter in her pocket Doris had suddenly grown wary.
10110{_}3608{_}Hart and Siddle would not mix, and her woman's intuition warned her that Siddle had chosen the tea-hour purposely in order to have an uninterrupted conversation with her.
10110{_}3609{_}She disliked Mr. Siddle, in a negative way, but the very nearness of the detective was stimulating.
10110{_}3610{_}Let Mr. Siddle come, then, and come alone!
10110{_}3611{_}"No, dad," she laughed.
10110{_}3612{_}"Mr. Hart's knowledge will be available to-morrow.
10110{_}3613{_}In his presence, poor Mr. Siddle would be dumb."
10110{_}3614{_}CHAPTER XIII  CONCERNING THEODOEE SIDDLE   Winter, being a cheerful cynic, had not erred when he appealed to that love of mystery which, especially if it is spiced with a hint of harmless intrigue, is innate in every feminine heart.
10110{_}3615{_}Indeed, he was so assured of the success of his somewhat dramatic move that as he walked to a rendezvous arranged with Superintendent Fowler on the Knoleworth road he reviewed carefully certain arguments meant to secure Doris's assistance.
10110{_}3616{_}Passing The Hollies, he smiled at the notion that Furneaux would undoubtedly have brought Grant to the conclave.
10110{_}3617{_}It was just the sort of difficult situation in which his colleague would have reveled.
10110{_}3618{_}But the Chief Inspector was more solid, more circumspect, even, singularly enough, more sensitive to the probable comments of a crusty judge if counsel for the defense contrived to elicit the facts.
10110{_}3619{_}"Anything fresh?"
10110{_}3620{_}inquired the superintendent, when a smart car drew up, and Winter entered.
10110{_}3621{_}Mr. Fowler was in plain clothes, and the blinds were half drawn.
10110{_}3622{_}No one could possibly recognize either of the occupants unless the car was halted, and the inquisitor literally thrust his head inside.
10110{_}3623{_}The motor was a private one, borrowed for the occasion.
10110{_}3624{_}"Yes, a little," said Winter, as the chauffeur put the engine in gear.
10110{_}3625{_}"Your man, Robinson, has been drawing Elkin, or Elkin drew him--I am not quite sure which, but think it matterless either way."
10110{_}3626{_}He sketched Robinson's activities briefly, but in sufficient outline.
10110{_}3627{_}"A new figure has come on the screen--Siddle, the chemist," he added thoughtfully.
10110{_}3628{_}"Siddle!"
10110{_}3629{_}Mr. Fowler was surprised.
10110{_}3630{_}"Why, he is supposed to be a model of the law-abiding citizen."
10110{_}3631{_}"I don't say he has lost his character in that respect," said Winter.
10110{_}3632{_}"Still, he puzzles me.
10110{_}3633{_}Elkin is a loud-mouthed fool.
10110{_}3634{_}The verbal bricks he hurls at Grant are generally half baked, and crumble into dust.
10110{_}3635{_}Hitherto, Siddle has tried to repress him, with a transparent honesty that rather worried me.
10110{_}3636{_}On Friday night, however, Siddle attacked Grant with poisoned arrows.
10110{_}3637{_}He did more damage in two minutes than Elkin could achieve in as many months."
10110{_}3638{_}"How?"
10110{_}3639{_}"He showed very clearly that Grant was guilty of gross bad taste in inviting Mr. Martin and his daughter to dinner that evening.
10110{_}3640{_}I'm inclined to agree with him, if the story has been told fairly.
10110{_}3641{_}But that is beside the main issue.
10110{_}3642{_}Siddle aroused the sleeping dogs of the village, and the pack is in full cry again.
10110{_}3643{_}Grant seems to have been popular here; he had almost recovered from the blow of Miss Melhuish's death by the straightforward speech he made before the inquest.
10110{_}3644{_}But Siddle threw him back into the mud by a few skillful words.
10110{_}3645{_}What is Siddle's record?
10110{_}3646{_}Is he a local man?"
10110{_}3647{_}"I think not.
10110{_}3648{_}Robinson can tell us."
10110{_}3649{_}"Robinson says he 'believes' Siddle is a widower.
10110{_}3650{_}That doesn't argue long and close knowledge."
10110{_}3651{_}"We must look into it.
10110{_}3652{_}Robinson has been stationed here four years.
10110{_}3653{_}Siddle is not old, but he has been in business in Steynholme more years than that.
10110{_}3654{_}But--you'll pardon me, I'm sure, Mr. Winter--may I take it that you are really interested in the chemist's history?"
10110{_}3655{_}The superintendent was perplexed, or he would not have adopted his professional method of semi-apologetic questions with a man from the C.I.D.
10110{_}3656{_}"I hardly know what I'm interested in," laughed Winter.
10110{_}3657{_}"Grant didn't kill the lady.
10110{_}3658{_}I shall be slow to credit Elkin with being the scoundrel he looks.
10110{_}3659{_}Siddle, and Tomlin, if you please, are regarded as starters in the Doris Martin Matrimonial Stakes, and I don't think Tomlin could ever murder anything but the King's English.
10110{_}3660{_}It is Siddle's _volte face_ that bothers me."
10110{_}3661{_}"Um!"
10110{_}3662{_}murmured Mr. Fowler.
10110{_}3663{_}He was not an uneducated man, but _volte face_, correctly pronounced, was unfamiliar in his ears.
10110{_}3664{_}"The change was so marked," went on the detective.
10110{_}3665{_}"I gather that Siddle is a stickler for charity and fair dealing.
10110{_}3666{_}He didn't abandon the role, of course.
10110{_}3667{_}It was the sheer ingenuity of his method that caught my attention.
10110{_}3668{_}So I simply catalogue him for research."
10110{_}3669{_}"Has Miss Martin promised to meet us?"
10110{_}3670{_}inquired the other, feeling that he was on the track of _volte face_.
10110{_}3671{_}"No.
10110{_}3672{_}But there she is!"
10110{_}3673{_}cried Winter.
10110{_}3674{_}"She has just heard the car.
10110{_}3675{_}Tell your chauffeur to slow up.
10110{_}3676{_}The road is empty otherwise.
10110{_}3677{_}By the way, you help her in.
10110{_}3678{_}She might be a bit shy of me, and I don't want a second's delay."
10110{_}3679{_}Winter's judgment was not at fault.
10110{_}3680{_}Doris _was_ feeling a trifle uncertain, seeing that she was about to encounter a complete stranger.
10110{_}3681{_}Moreover, she had come a good half mile from the shop whence the cakes for tea were to be procured at the back door, and as a favor.
10110{_}3682{_}Her eyes were fixed on the slowing car with a timid anxiety that betrayed no small degree of doubt as to the outcome of this Sunday afternoon escapade.
10110{_}3683{_}She was pale and nervous.
10110{_}3684{_}At that moment Doris wished herself safe at home again.
10110{_}3685{_}"One word," broke in the superintendent hurriedly.
10110{_}3686{_}"Why are you so sure that Grant is innocent, Mr.
10110{_}3687{_}Winter?"
10110{_}3688{_}"I'm sure of nothing with regard to this case.
10110{_}3689{_}But I have great faith in Furneaux's flair for the true scent.
10110{_}3690{_}It has never failed yet."
10110{_}3691{_}Mr. Fowler wished his companion would not use such uncommon words.
10110{_}3692{_}However, he got out, and took off his hat with a courteous sweep.
10110{_}3693{_}Doris had to look twice at him.
10110{_}3694{_}Hitherto, she had always seen him in uniform.
10110{_}3695{_}Winter smiled at the unmistakable expression of relief in her face.
10110{_}3696{_}She was almost self-possessed as she took the seat by his side.
10110{_}3697{_}"Good day, Mr. Winter," she said.
10110{_}3698{_}"Mr. Franklin, please.
10110{_}3699{_}Better become used to my pseudonym....
10110{_}3700{_}Plenty of room for your feet, Mr. Fowler?
10110{_}3701{_}That's it.
10110{_}3702{_}Now we're comfy.
10110{_}3703{_}The chauffeur will bring us back here in half an hour, Miss Martin.
10110{_}3704{_}Will that suit your convenience?"
10110{_}3705{_}"Oh, yes.
10110{_}3706{_}I am free till nearly four o'clock.
10110{_}3707{_}We have a guest to tea then."
10110{_}3708{_}"I have a well-developed bump of curiosity these days.
10110{_}3709{_}Who is it, may I ask?"
10110{_}3710{_}"Mr. Siddle, the local chemist."
10110{_}3711{_}"Indeed.
10110{_}3712{_}An old friend, I suppose?"
10110{_}3713{_}"We have known him seven years, ever since he came to Steynholme."
10110{_}3714{_}"Ah.
10110{_}3715{_}He is not a native of the place?"
10110{_}3716{_}"No.
10110{_}3717{_}He bought Mr. Benson's business.
10110{_}3718{_}He's a Londoner, I believe."
10110{_}3719{_}"Is there--a Mrs.
10110{_}3720{_}Siddle?"
10110{_}3721{_}"No.
10110{_}3722{_}I--er--that is to say, gossip has it that he was married, but his wife died."
10110{_}3723{_}"He doesn't speak of her?
10110{_}3724{_}Is that it?
10110{_}3725{_}One would have thought that in a house where he is well known--"  "We don't really know him well.
10110{_}3726{_}No one does, I think."
10110{_}3727{_}"You've invited him to tea, at any rate," laughed Winter.
10110{_}3728{_}"No," said Doris.
10110{_}3729{_}"He invited himself.
10110{_}3730{_}At least, so I gathered from dad."
10110{_}3731{_}"Ah, well.
10110{_}3732{_}He feels lonely, no doubt, and wishes to chat about recent strange events in Steynholme.
10110{_}3733{_}And that brings me to the reason why I sought this chat under such peculiar conditions.
10110{_}3734{_}You realize my handicap, Miss Martin?
10110{_}3735{_}If I were seen talking to you, or even entering your house as apart from the post office, people would begin to wonder.
10110{_}3736{_}You follow that, don't you?"
10110{_}3737{_}Yes, Doris did follow it.
10110{_}3738{_}What she did not follow was the veiled admiration in Superintendent Fowler's glance at the detective.
10110{_}3739{_}Those few inconsequential questions had shed a flood of light on Siddle's past and present, yet the informant was blissfully unaware of their real purport.
10110{_}3740{_}And the way was opened so deftly.
10110{_}3741{_}The purchase of a chemist's business would almost certainly be negotiated through a local lawyer.
10110{_}3742{_}Let him be found, and Siddle's pre-Steynholme days could be "looked into," as the police phrase has it.
10110{_}3743{_}The superintendent had the rare merit of being candid with himself.
10110{_}3744{_}He had no previous experience of Scotland Yard men or methods, and was inclined to be skeptical about Furneaux.
10110{_}3745{_}But Winter's prompt use of a chance opening, and the restraint which cut off the investigation before the girl could suspect any ulterior motive, displayed a technique which the Sussex Constabulary had few opportunities of acquiring.
10110{_}3746{_}"Now, Miss Martin," began Winter, "if ever you have the misfortune to fall ill--touch wood, please--and call in a doctor, you'll tell him the facts, eh?"
10110{_}3747{_}"Why consult him at all, if I don't?"
10110{_}3748{_}she smiled.
10110{_}3749{_}"Exactly.
10110{_}3750{_}To-day I'm somewhat in the position of a Harley-street specialist, summoned to assist an eminent local practitioner in Dr. Fowler.
10110{_}3751{_}That's a sort of gentle preliminary, leading up to the disagreeable duty of putting some questions of a personal nature.
10110{_}3752{_}What you may answer will not go beyond ourselves.
10110{_}3753{_}I promise you that.
10110{_}3754{_}You will not be quoted, or requested to prove your statements.
10110{_}3755{_}Such a thing would be absurd.
10110{_}3756{_}If I were really a doctor, and you needed my advice, you might easily describe your symptoms all wrong.
10110{_}3757{_}It would be my business to listen, and deduce the truth, and I would never dream of rating you for having misled me.
10110{_}3758{_}You see my point?"
10110{_}3759{_}"Yes, but Mr.
10110{_}3760{_}Win--Mr. Franklin, I know nothing whatever about the murder."
10110{_}3761{_}"I'm sure you don't.
10110{_}3762{_}It was a wicked trick of Fate that took you to Mr. Grant's garden last Monday night."
10110{_}3763{_}"It was really an astronomical almanac," retorted Doris, who now felt a growing confidence in this nice-spoken official.
10110{_}3764{_}"Sirius is a star remarkable for its beautiful changing lights, and on Monday evening was at its best.
10110{_}3765{_}I think I ought to explain," and she blushed delightfully, "that the village gossip about Mr. Grant and me is entirely mistaken.
10110{_}3766{_}We are not--well, I had better use plain English--we are not lovers.
10110{_}3767{_}My father and I are just on close, friendly terms with Mr. Grant.
10110{_}3768{_}I--my position hardly warrants even that relationship with an author of some distinction.
10110{_}3769{_}But please set aside any notion of us as likely to become engaged.
10110{_}3770{_}For one thing, it is preposterous.
10110{_}3771{_}For another, I shall not leave my father."
10110{_}3772{_}Poor Doris!
10110{_}3773{_}She little guessed how accurately this skilled student of human nature read the hidden thought behind that vehement protest.
10110{_}3774{_}Even the note of vague rebellion against social disabilities was pathetic yet illuminating.
10110{_}3775{_}Of course, he took her quite seriously.
10110{_}3776{_}"Let us keep to the hard road of fact," he said.
10110{_}3777{_}"What you really mean is that Mr. Grant has never made love to you.
10110{_}3778{_}But I must be candid, young lady.
10110{_}3779{_}There is no earthly reason why he shouldn't, though I could name offhand half a dozen why he should.... Well, well, I must not pay compliments.
10110{_}3780{_}My friend, Mr. Furneaux, can manage that with much greater facility, being half a Frenchman.
10110{_}3781{_}And now I'm going to say an unpleasant thing.
10110{_}3782{_}I ask your forgiveness in advance.
10110{_}3783{_}Both Mr. Furneaux and I agree in the opinion that your imaginary love affair is indissolubly bound up with the mystery of Miss Melhuish's death.
10110{_}3784{_}In a word, I have brought you here today to discuss your prospective marriage, and nothing else.
10110{_}3785{_}That astonishes you, eh?
10110{_}3786{_}Well, it's the truth, as I shall proceed to make clear.
10110{_}3787{_}There's a Mr. Fred Elkin, for instance--"  Doris uttered a little laugh of dismay.
10110{_}3788{_}Winter's emphatic words had astounded her, but the horse-dealer's name acted as comic relief.
10110{_}3789{_}"I can't bear the man," she protested.
10110{_}3790{_}"I have no doubt.
10110{_}3791{_}But you ought to know that he is loudly proclaiming his determination to marry you before the year is out."
10110{_}3792{_}The girl's face reddened again, and her eyes sparkled.
10110{_}3793{_}"I wouldn't marry him if he were a peer of the realm," she said indignantly.
10110{_}3794{_}"Quite so.
10110{_}3795{_}But he is an avowed suitor.
10110{_}3796{_}Now don't be vexed.
10110{_}3797{_}Has he never declared his intentions to _you_?"
10110{_}3798{_}"He would never dare.
10110{_}3799{_}I sing and act a little, at village concerts and dramatic performances, and he has annoyed me at times by an officious pretense that he was deputed by my father to see me home.
10110{_}3800{_}I came here quite a little girl, so people learnt to use my Christian name.
10110{_}3801{_}I don't object to it at all.
10110{_}3802{_}But I simply hate hearing it on Mr. Elkin's lips."
10110{_}3803{_}"Exit Fred!"
10110{_}3804{_}said Winter solemnly.
10110{_}3805{_}"Next!"
10110{_}3806{_}Doris, after a period of calm, was now profoundly uncomfortable.
10110{_}3807{_}This kind of prying was the last thing she had expected.
10110{_}3808{_}She had come prepared to defend Grant, but, beyond one exceedingly personal reference, the detective had studiously shut him out of the conversation.
10110{_}3809{_}"What am I to say?"
10110{_}3810{_}she cried.
10110{_}3811{_}"Do you want a list of all the young men who make sheep's eyes at me?"
10110{_}3812{_}"No.
10110{_}3813{_}I can get that from the Census Bureau.
10110{_}3814{_}Come, now, Miss Martin.
10110{_}3815{_}_You_ know.
10110{_}3816{_}Has any man in the village led you to suspect, shall we put it?
10110{_}3817{_}that sometime or other, he might ask you to become his wife?"
10110{_}3818{_}Lo, and behold!
10110{_}3819{_}Doris's pretty eyes filled with tears.
10110{_}3820{_}Superintendent Fowler was so pleased at hearing Scotland Yard introducing a parenthetical query into its sentences that he, sitting opposite, was taken aback when Winter said in a fatherly way:  "I've been rather clumsy, I'm afraid.
10110{_}3821{_}But it cannot be helped.
10110{_}3822{_}I must go blundering on.
10110{_}3823{_}I'm groping in the dark, you know, but it's a thousand pities I shall have to tread on _your_ toes."

10110{_}3825{_}"I hate to put my thoughts into words.
10110{_}3826{_}That's all.
10110{_}3827{_}There _is_ a man whom I'm--afraid of."

10110{_}3829{_}She turned on Winter a face of sudden awe.

10110{_}3831{_}she said wonderingly, and sheer bewilderment dried her tears.
10110{_}3832{_}"My business is nine-tenths guesswork.

10110{_}3837{_}"Yes."
10110{_}3838{_}"Elkin--I must drag him in again for an instant--pretends that the commotion aroused in the village by this murder would incline you favorably to a proposal of marriage.
10110{_}3839{_}Mr. Siddle may have discovered some virtue in the theory."
10110{_}3840{_}"Did Mr. Elkin really hint that I needed _him_ as a shield?"
10110{_}3841{_}Doris was genuinely angry now.
10110{_}3842{_}She little imagined that Winter was playing on her emotions with a master hand.
10110{_}3843{_}"Don't waste any wrath on Elkin," he soothed her.
10110{_}3844{_}"The fellow isn't worth it.
10110{_}3845{_}But his crude idea might be developed more subtly by an abler man."

10110{_}3847{_}Winter relapsed into silence for a while.
10110{_}3848{_}The car was running through a charming countryside, and a glimpse of the sea was obtainable from the crest of each hill.
10110{_}3849{_}Mr. Fowler was too circumspect to break in on the thread of his coadjutor's thoughts.
10110{_}3850{_}The inquiry had taken a curious turn, and was momentarily beyond his grasp.

10110{_}3853{_}"I can invite you to tea."
10110{_}3854{_}Alas!
10110{_}3855{_}that won't serve our ends.

10110{_}3860{_}"I think it bad, most disagreeable."
10110{_}3861{_}"You won't find the position so awkward if you are playing a part.
10110{_}3862{_}And that is what I want--a bit of clever acting.

10110{_}3864{_}You know the kind of thing I mean.

10110{_}3866{_}You will annoy Siddle, and a cautious man in a temper becomes less cautious.
10110{_}3867{_}Force him to avow his real thoughts.
10110{_}3868{_}You will learn something, trust me."
10110{_}3869{_}"About what?"
10110{_}3870{_}There were no tears in Doris's eyes.
10110{_}3871{_}They were wide open in wonderment.
10110{_}3872{_}"About his attitude to this tragedy.
10110{_}3873{_}Do this, and you will be giving Mr. Grant the greatest possible help.
10110{_}3874{_}He needs it.
10110{_}3875{_}Next Wednesday, at the adjourned inquest, he will be put on the rack.
10110{_}3876{_}Ingerman will fee counsel to be vindictive, merciless.
10110{_}3877{_}Such men are to be hired.
10110{_}3878{_}Their reputation is built up on the slaughter of reputations.
10110{_}3879{_}I want to understand Siddle before Wednesday.
10110{_}3880{_}By the way, what's his other name?"
10110{_}3881{_}"Theodore."
10110{_}3882{_}"Theodore Siddle.
10110{_}3883{_}Unusual.
10110{_}3884{_}Well, your half hour is nearly up.
10110{_}3885{_}Will you do what I ask?"
10110{_}3886{_}"I'll try.

10110{_}3893{_}"Because it is the hardest thing in the world for a woman to be single-minded, in the limited sense of concentration, I mean.
10110{_}3894{_}Focus your wits on Siddle to-day.
10110{_}3895{_}I don't suggest any plan.

10110{_}3899{_}"Yes.

10110{_}3902{_}She was troubled and serious, very serious.

10110{_}3907{_}All this is preparatory for Wednesday."

10110{_}3910{_}Not at present.

10110{_}3912{_}The car had stopped.
10110{_}3913{_}It sped on when Doris alighted.
10110{_}3914{_}She would be home with her cakes at three o'clock, and Mr. Martin would never have noticed her absence.
10110{_}3915{_}"A fine bit of work, if I may say so," exclaimed Fowler appreciatively.
10110{_}3916{_}"But I am jiggered if I can imagine what you're driving at."
10110{_}3917{_}Winter was cutting the end off a big cigar.

10110{_}3920{_}After five days, where are we, Mr. Fowler?
10110{_}3921{_}In the dark, plus a brigand's hat and hair.
10110{_}3922{_}But there's a queer belief in some parts of England that a phosphorescent gleam shows at night over a deep pool in which a dead body lies.
10110{_}3923{_}That's just how I feel about Siddle.
10110{_}3924{_}The man's an enigma.
10110{_}3925{_}What sort of place is Steynholme for a chemist of his capacities?
10110{_}3926{_}Dr. Foxton has the highest regard for him professionally, and I'm told he doctors people for miles around.
10110{_}3927{_}Yet he lives the life of a recluse.
10110{_}3928{_}An old woman comes by day to prepare his meals, and tidy the house and shop.
10110{_}3929{_}His sole relaxation is an hour of an evening in the village inn, his visits there being uninterrupted since the murder.
10110{_}3930{_}He was there on the night of the murder, too.
10110{_}3931{_}For the rest, he is alone, shut off from the world.
10110{_}3932{_}Without knowing it, he's going to fall into deep waters to-day, and he'll emit sparks, or I'm a Chinaman....
10110{_}3933{_}I'll leave you here.
10110{_}3934{_}Good-by!
10110{_}3935{_}See you on Tuesday, after lunch."
10110{_}3936{_}The superintendent drove on alone.
10110{_}3937{_}He pondered the Steynholme affair in all its bearings, but mostly did he weigh up Winter and Furneaux.
10110{_}3938{_}At last, he sighed.
10110{_}3939{_}"London ways, and London books, and London detectives!"
10110{_}3940{_}he muttered.
10110{_}3941{_}"We're not up to date in Sussex.
10110{_}3942{_}Now, if I could please myself, I'd be hot-foot after Elkin.
10110{_}3943{_}I see what Winter has in his mind, but surely Elkin fills the bill, and Siddle doesn't.... What was that word--volt what!"
10110{_}3944{_}Doris was lucky.
10110{_}3945{_}She met Mr. Siddle as she emerged from the back passage to the cake-shop.
10110{_}3946{_}Resolving instantly that if an unpleasant thing had to be done it should at least be done well, she smiled brightly.
10110{_}3947{_}"See what you have driven me to--breaking the Sabbath," she cried, holding up the bag of cakes.
10110{_}3948{_}"Tea and bread-and-butter with you would be a feast for the gods," said Siddle.
10110{_}3949{_}"Now you're adapting Omar Khayyam."
10110{_}3950{_}"Who's he?"
10110{_}3951{_}"A Persian poet of long ago."
10110{_}3952{_}"I never read poetry.
10110{_}3953{_}But, if your tastes lie that way, I'll accomplish some more adaptation."
10110{_}3954{_}"Oh, no, please.
10110{_}3955{_}Cakes for you, Mr. Siddle; poets for giddy young things like me."
10110{_}3956{_}There was a sting in the words.
10110{_}3957{_}Doris preened herself on having carried out the detective's instructions to the letter thus far.
10110{_}3958{_}Arrived in the house she found her father still in the garden, examining some larvae under a microscope.
10110{_}3959{_}He looked severe rather than studious.
10110{_}3960{_}He might have been an omnipotent being who had detected a malefactor in a criminal act.
10110{_}3961{_}Was Steynholme and its secret felon being regarded in that way by the providence which, for some inscrutable purpose, permitted, yet would infallibly punish, a dreadful murder?
10110{_}3962{_}She was a girl of devout mind, and the notion was appalling in its direct application to current events.
10110{_}3963{_}In the meantime the chemist, evidently taking a Sunday afternoon constitutional, came on Winter, who was leaning on a wall of the bridge and looking down stream--Grant's house being on the left.
10110{_}3964{_}He would have passed, in his wonted unobtrusive way, but the detective hailed him with a cheery "Good day, Mr. Siddle.
10110{_}3965{_}Are you a fisherman?"
10110{_}3966{_}"No, Mr. Franklin, I'm not," he answered.
10110{_}3967{_}"Well, now, I'm surprised.
10110{_}3968{_}You are just the sort of man whom I should expect to find attached to a rod and line--even watching a float."
10110{_}3969{_}"I tried once when I was younger, but I could neither impale a worm nor extract a hook.
10110{_}3970{_}My gorge rose against either practice.
10110{_}3971{_}I am a vegetarian, for the same reason.
10110{_}3972{_}If it were not for this disturbing tragedy you would have heard Hobbs, the butcher, rallying me about my rabbit-meat, as he calls my food."
10110{_}3973{_}"Well, well!"
10110{_}3974{_}laughed Winter.
10110{_}3975{_}"Your ideas and mine clash in some respects.
10110{_}3976{_}I look on a well-grilled steak as a gift from Heaven, and after it, or before it--I don't care which--let me have three hours whipping a good trout stream.
10110{_}3977{_}With the right cast of flies I could show a fine bag from this very stretch of water."
10110{_}3978{_}"Why not ask Mr. Grant's permission?
10110{_}3979{_}It would be interesting to learn whether he will allow others to try their luck."
10110{_}3980{_}Mr. Siddle strolled on.
10110{_}3981{_}Winter bent over, keen to discern the gray-backed fish which must be lurking in those clear depths and rippling shallows.
10110{_}3982{_}CHAPTER XIV  ON BOTH SIDES OF THE BIVEE   The sun, transmuted into Greenwich time, exercised an extraordinary influence on the seemingly humdrum life of Steynholme that day.
10110{_}3983{_}A few minutes after three o'clock--just too late to observe either Winter or Siddle--P.C.
10110{_}3984{_}Robinson strolled forth from his cottage.
10110{_}3985{_}He glanced up the almost deserted high-street, in which every rounded cobble and white flagstone radiated heat.
10110{_}3986{_}A high-class automobile had dashed past twice in forty minutes, but the pace was on the borderland of doubt, so the guardian of the public weal had contented himself with recording its number on the return journey.
10110{_}3987{_}But his thoughts were far a-field from joyriders, stray cattle, hawkers without licenses, and other similar small fry which come into the constabulary net.
10110{_}3988{_}It would be a feather in his cap if he could only strike the trail of the veritable Steynholme murderer.
10110{_}3989{_}The entrancing notion possessed him morning, noon, and night.
10110{_}3990{_}Mrs. Robinson declared that it even dominated his dreams.
10110{_}3991{_}Robinson was sharp.
10110{_}3992{_}He knew quite well that the brains of the London detectives held some elusive quality which he personally lacked.
10110{_}3993{_}They seemed to peer into the heart of a thing so wisely and thoroughly.
10110{_}3994{_}He did not share Superintendent Fowler's somewhat derogatory estimate of Furneaux, with whom he was much better acquainted than was his superior officer, while Chief Inspector Winter's repute stood so high that it might not be questioned.
10110{_}3995{_}Still, to the best of his belief, the case had beaten both these doughty representatives of Scotland Yard; there was yet a chance for the humble police-constable; so Robinson squared his shoulders, seamed his brows, and marched majestically down the Knoleworth road.
10110{_}3996{_}He had an eye for The Hollies, of course, though neither he nor anybody else could discern more than the bare edge of the lawn from bridge or road, owing to the dense screen of evergreen trees and shrubs planted by the tenant who remodeled the property.
10110{_}3997{_}But the spot where the body of Adelaide Melhuish was drawn ashore was visible, and the sight of it started a dim thesis in the policeman's mind which took definite shape during less than an hour's stroll.
10110{_}3998{_}Thus, at four o'clock exactly, he was pulling the bell at The Hollies.
10110{_}3999{_}Almost simultaneously, Mr. Siddle knocked modestly on the private door of the post office, to reach which one had to pass down a narrow yard.
10110{_}4000{_}"Mr. Grant at home?"
10110{_}4001{_}inquired Robinson, when Minnie appeared.
10110{_}4002{_}Yes, the master was on the lawn with Mr. Hart.
10110{_}4003{_}The policeman found the two there, seated in chairs with awnings.
10110{_}4004{_}They had been discussing, of all things in the world, the futurist craze in painting.
10110{_}4005{_}Hart held by it, but Grant carried bigger guns in real knowledge of the artist's limitations as well as his privileges.
10110{_}4006{_}Hart was the first to notice the newcomer's presence, and greeted him joyously.
10110{_}4007{_}"Come along, Robinson, and manacle this reprobate," he shouted.
10110{_}4008{_}"He's nothing but a narrow-minded pre-Rafaelite.
10110{_}4009{_}A period in prison will dust the cobwebs out of his attic."
10110{_}4010{_}"Hello, Robinson!"
10110{_}4011{_}said, Grant.
10110{_}4012{_}"Anything stirring?"
10110{_}4013{_}"Not much, sir.
10110{_}4014{_}I just popped in to ask if you remembered exactly how the body was roped?"
10110{_}4015{_}"Indeed, I do not.
10110{_}4016{_}Some incidents of that horrible half hour have gone into a sad jumble.
10110{_}4017{_}I recollect you calling attention to the matter, but what your point was I really cannot say now.
10110{_}4018{_}Perhaps it may come back if you explain."
10110{_}4019{_}"Well, we don't seem to be making a great deal of progress, sir, and I was wondering whether you two gentlemen might help.
10110{_}4020{_}I don't want it mentioned.
10110{_}4021{_}I'm taking a line of me own."
10110{_}4022{_}Grant repressed a smile.
10110{_}4023{_}He recalled well enough the first "line" the policeman took, and the mischief it had caused.
10110{_}4024{_}Being an even-minded person, however, he admitted that his own behavior had not been above suspicion on the day the crime was discovered.
10110{_}4025{_}In allotting blame, as between Robinson and himself, the proportion was six of one and half a dozen of the other.
10110{_}4026{_}"Propound, justiciary," said Hart.
10110{_}4027{_}"You've started well, anyhow.
10110{_}4028{_}The connection between a line and a rope should be obvious even to a judge.... As a pipe-opener, have a drink!"
10110{_}4029{_}Robinson had removed his helmet, and was flourishing a red handkerchief, not without cause, the day being really very hot.
10110{_}4030{_}"Not for a few minutes, thank you, sir," said the policeman.
10110{_}4031{_}"May I ask Bates for a sack and a cord?"
10110{_}4032{_}He went to the kitchen.
10110{_}4033{_}Hart was "tickled to death," he vowed.
10110{_}4034{_}"We are about to witness the reconstruction of the crime, a procedure which the French delight in, and the intellect of France is a hundred years ahead of our effete civilization," he chortled.
10110{_}4035{_}Grant was not so pleased.
10110{_}4036{_}The memory of a distressing vision was beginning to blur, and this ponderous policeman must come and revive it.
10110{_}4037{_}Yet, even he grew interested when Robinson illustrated a nebulous idea by knotting a clothesline around a sack stuffed with straw, having brought Bates to bear him out in the matter of accuracy.
10110{_}4038{_}"There you are, gentlemen!"
10110{_}4039{_}he said, puffing after the slight exertion.
10110{_}4040{_}"That's the way of it.
10110{_}4041{_}How does it strike you?"
10110{_}4042{_}"It's what a sailor calls two half hitches," commented Hart instantly.
10110{_}4043{_}"A very serviceable knot, which will resist to the full strength of the rope."
10110{_}4044{_}"We have no sailors in Steynholme, sir," said the policeman.
10110{_}4045{_}"Oh, it's used regularly by tradesmen," put in Grant.
10110{_}4046{_}"A draper, or grocer--any man accustomed to tying parcels securely, in fact--will fashion that knot nine times out of ten."
10110{_}4047{_}"How about a--a farmer, sir?"
10110{_}4048{_}That was as near as Robinson dared to go to "horse-dealer."
10110{_}4049{_}"I think a farmer would be more likely to adopt a timber hitch, which is made in several ways.
10110{_}4050{_}Here are samples."
10110{_}4051{_}And Grant busied himself with rope and sack.
10110{_}4052{_}Robinson watched closely.
10110{_}4053{_}"Yes," he nodded.
10110{_}4054{_}"I've seen those knots in a farmyard.... Well, it's something--not much--but a trifle better than nothing.... All right, Bates.
10110{_}4055{_}You can take 'em away."
10110{_}4056{_}"Have you shown that knot to Mr.
10110{_}4057{_}Furneaux?"
10110{_}4058{_}inquired Grant.
10110{_}4059{_}"No, sir.
10110{_}4060{_}I've kept that up me sleeve, as the sayin' is."
10110{_}4061{_}"But why?"
10110{_}4062{_}Robinson shuffled uneasily on his feet.
10110{_}4063{_}"These Scotland Yard men will hardly listen to a uniformed constable, sir," he said.
10110{_}4064{_}"I'll tell 'em all about it at the inquest on Wednesday."
10110{_}4065{_}"In effect, John P. Robinson he sez they didn't know everythin' down in Judee," quoted Hart.
10110{_}4066{_}"You've got my name pat," grinned the policeman, whose Christian names were "John Price."
10110{_}4067{_}"My name is Walter, not Patrick," retorted Hart.
10110{_}4068{_}Robinson continued to smile, though he failed to grasp the joke until late that evening.
10110{_}4069{_}"Did you make up that verse straight off, sir," he asked.
10110{_}4070{_}"No.
10110{_}4071{_}It's a borrowed plume, plucked from an American quill pen."
10110{_}4072{_}Hart gave "plume" a French sound, and Robinson was puzzled to know why Grant bade his friend stop profaning a peaceful Sunday afternoon.
10110{_}4073{_}"You'll have a glass of beer now?"
10110{_}4074{_}went on the host.
10110{_}4075{_}"I don't mind if I do, sir, though it's tea-time, and I make it a rule on Sundays to have tea with the missis.
10110{_}4076{_}A policeman's hours are broken up, and his wife hardly ever knows when to have a meal ready."
10110{_}4077{_}Minnie was summoned.
10110{_}4078{_}It took her a couple of minutes to draw the beer from a cool cellar.
10110{_}4079{_}So it chanced that when Doris led Mr. Siddle to the edge of the cliff about twenty-five minutes past four, the first thing they saw was the local police-constable on the lawn of The Hollies putting down a gill of "best Sussex" at a draught.
10110{_}4080{_}"Well!"
10110{_}4081{_}cried the chemist icily, "I wonder what Superintendent Fowler would say to that if he knew it?"
10110{_}4082{_}"What is there particularly wrong about Robinson drinking a glass of beer?"
10110{_}4083{_}demanded Doris, more alive to the insinuation in Siddle's words than was quite permissible under the role imposed on her by Winter.
10110{_}4084{_}She waved her hand to the party on the lawn.
10110{_}4085{_}Grant, whose eyes ever roved in that direction, had seen her white muslin dress the moment she appeared.
10110{_}4086{_}"Who the deuce is that with Miss Martin?"
10110{_}4087{_}he said, returning her signal.
10110{_}4088{_}"Siddle, the chemist," announced Robinson, not too well pleased himself at being "spotted" so openly.
10110{_}4089{_}"Well, gentlemen, I'll be off," and he vanished by the side path through the laurels.
10110{_}4090{_}"Siddle!"
10110{_}4091{_}repeated Grant vexedly.
10110{_}4092{_}"So it is.
10110{_}4093{_}And she dislikes the man, for some reason."
10110{_}4094{_}"Let's go and rescue the fair maid," prompted Hart.
10110{_}4095{_}"No, no.
10110{_}4096{_}If Doris wanted me she would let me know."
10110{_}4097{_}"How?
10110{_}4098{_}At the top of her voice?"
10110{_}4099{_}"You're far too curious, Wally."
10110{_}4100{_}"Semaphore, of course," drawled Hart.
10110{_}4101{_}"When are you going to marry the girl, Jack!"
10110{_}4102{_}"As soon as this infernal business has blown over."
10110{_}4103{_}"You haven't asked her, I gather?"
10110{_}4104{_}"No."
10110{_}4105{_}"Tell me when you do, and I'll hie me to London town, though in torrid June.
10110{_}4106{_}You're unbearable in love."
10110{_}4107{_}"The lash of your wit cuts deeply sometimes," said Grant quietly.
10110{_}4108{_}"Dash it all, old chap, I was talking at random.
10110{_}4109{_}Very well.
10110{_}4110{_}I'll do penance in sackcloth and ashes by remaining here, and applauding your poetic efforts.
10110{_}4111{_}I'll even help.
10110{_}4112{_}I'm a dab at sonnets."
10110{_}4113{_}Meanwhile, Mr. Siddle had regained his poise.
10110{_}4114{_}"I meant nothing offensive to the donor of the beer," he said, tuning his voice to an apologetic note.
10110{_}4115{_}"But I take it Robinson is conducting certain inquiries, and I imagine that his superiors demand a degree of circumspection in such conditions.
10110{_}4116{_}That is all."
10110{_}4117{_}"Surely you do not rank with the stupid crowd in its suspicions of Mr.
10110{_}4118{_}Grant?"
10110{_}4119{_}said the girl.
10110{_}4120{_}"I'm pleased to think you refuse to class me with the gossip-mongers of Steynholme, Doris," was the guarded answer.
10110{_}4121{_}There had been no reference to the murder during tea, which was served as soon as the chemist came in.
10110{_}4122{_}The visitor had tabled a copy of a current medical journal containing an article on the therapeutic qualities of honey, so the talk was lifted at once into an atmosphere far removed from crime.
10110{_}4123{_}Doris was grateful for his tact.
10110{_}4124{_}When her father went to the office she brought Mr. Siddle into the garden solely in pursuance of her promise to the detective, though convinced that there would be no outcome save a few labored compliments to herself.
10110{_}4125{_}And now, by accident, as it were, the death of Adelaide Melhuish thrust itself into their conversation.
10110{_}4126{_}Perhaps it was her fault.
10110{_}4127{_}"No," she said candidly.
10110{_}4128{_}"No one who has known you for seven years, Mr. Siddle, could possibly accuse you of spreading scandal."
10110{_}4129{_}"Seven years!
10110{_}4130{_}Is it so long since I came to Steynholme?
10110{_}4131{_}Sometimes, it appears an age, but more often I fancy the calendar must be in error.
10110{_}4132{_}Why, it seems only the other day that I saw you in a short frock, bowling a hoop."
10110{_}4133{_}"A tom-boy occupation," laughed Doris.
10110{_}4134{_}"But dad encouraged that and skipping, as the best possible means of exercise."
10110{_}4135{_}"He was right.
10110{_}4136{_}Look how straight and svelte you are!
10110{_}4137{_}Few, if any, among our community can have watched your progress to womanhood as closely as I.
10110{_}4138{_}You see, living opposite, as I do, I kept track of you more intimately than your other neighbors."
10110{_}4139{_}Siddle was trimming his sails cleverly.
10110{_}4140{_}The concluding sentence robbed his earlier comments of their sentimental import.
10110{_}4141{_}"If we live long enough we may even see each other in the sere and yellow leaf," said Doris flippantly.
10110{_}4142{_}"I would ask no greater happiness," came the quiet reply, and Doris could have bitten her tongue for according him that unguarded opening.
10110{_}4143{_}Suddenly availing herself of the advice which the detective, like Hamlet, had given to the players, she gazed musingly at the fair panorama of The Hollies and its gardens, with the two young men seated on the lawn.
10110{_}4144{_}By this time Minnie was staging tea, and the picture looked idyllic enough.
10110{_}4145{_}Doris saw, out of the tail of her eye, that her companion was watching her furtively, though apparently absorbed in the scene.
10110{_}4146{_}He moistened his thin lips with his tongue.
10110{_}4147{_}"As a study in contrasts, that would be hard to beat," he said, after a long pause.
10110{_}4148{_}"Contrasts!"
10110{_}4149{_}she echoed.
10110{_}4150{_}"Well, yes.
10110{_}4151{_}Even an uncontentious man like myself can hardly fail to compare Sunday afternoon with Tuesday morning."
10110{_}4152{_}"Why not Monday night?"
10110{_}4153{_}she flashed.
10110{_}4154{_}"Monday night, in part, remains a mystery yet to be unveiled.
10110{_}4155{_}I blot Monday night from my mind.
10110{_}4156{_}I have no alternative, being on the jury which has to arrive at a just verdict.
10110{_}4157{_}Now, if Fred Elkin were here, he would foam at the mouth."
10110{_}4158{_}"Happily, Fred Elkin is _not_ here."
10110{_}4159{_}"Ah, I am glad, glad, to hear you say that.
10110{_}4160{_}You don't like him?"
10110{_}4161{_}"I detest him."
10110{_}4162{_}"He makes out, to put it mildly, that you are great friends."
10110{_}4163{_}"You will oblige me by contradicting the statement.
10110{_}4164{_}Or--no.
10110{_}4165{_}One treats that sort of man with contempt."
10110{_}4166{_}"I agree with you most heartily.
10110{_}4167{_}I'm sorry I ever mentioned him."
10110{_}4168{_}Yet Doris was well aware that the chemist had dragged in Elkin by the scruff of the neck, probably for the sake of getting him disposed of thoroughly and for all time.
10110{_}4169{_}Rather on the tiptoe of expectation, she awaited the next move.
10110{_}4170{_}It was slow in coming, so again she looked wistfully at the distant tea-drinkers.
10110{_}4171{_}She found slight difficulty in carrying out this portion of the stage directions.
10110{_}4172{_}Truth to tell, she would gleefully have gone and joined them.
10110{_}4173{_}Siddle was not altogether at ease.
10110{_}4174{_}The conversation was too spasmodic to suit his purpose.
10110{_}4175{_}Though slow of speech he was nimble of brain, and, knowing Doris so well, he had anticipated a livelier duel of wits.
10110{_}4176{_}In all likelihood, he cursed the tea-party on the lawn.
10110{_}4177{_}He had not foreseen this drawback.
10110{_}4178{_}But, being a masterful man, he tackled the situation boldly.
10110{_}4179{_}"I seized the opportunity of a friendly chat with you to-day, Doris," he went on, leaning over the fence to inhale the scent of a briar rose.
10110{_}4180{_}"The story runs through the village that you and your father dined at The Hollies on Friday evening.
10110{_}4181{_}Is that true?"
10110{_}4182{_}Now, Doris had it on reliable authority that Siddle himself had been the runner who spread that story, and the knowledge steeled her heart against him.
10110{_}4183{_}"Yes," she said composedly.
10110{_}4184{_}"It was kind and neighborly of you to accept the invitation, but a mistake."
10110{_}4185{_}She turned and faced him.
10110{_}4186{_}His expression was baffling.
10110{_}4187{_}She thought she saw in his sallow, clean-cut features the shadow of a confident smile.
10110{_}4188{_}"You mean that this horrid murder should make some difference in the friendship between ourselves and Mr.
10110{_}4189{_}Grant?"
10110{_}4190{_}she cried.
10110{_}4191{_}"Yes.
10110{_}4192{_}To you, though to no one else would I speak so plainly, I have no hesitation in saying that Mr. Grant is far, very far, from being clear of responsibility in that matter.
10110{_}4193{_}Three days from now you will understand what I mean.
10110{_}4194{_}Evidence will be forthcoming which will put him in a most unenviable light.
10110{_}4195{_}I am not alleging, or even hinting, that he may be deemed guilty of actual crime.
10110{_}4196{_}That is for the law to determine.
10110{_}4197{_}But I do tell you emphatically that his present heedless attitude will give place to anxiety and dejection.
10110{_}4198{_}It cannot be otherwise.
10110{_}4199{_}A somewhat sordid history will be revealed, and his pretense that relations between him and the dead woman ceased three years ago will vanish into thin air.
10110{_}4200{_}Believe me, Doris, I am actuated by no motive in this matter other than a desire to further your welfare.
10110{_}4201{_}I cannot bear even to think of your name being associated, in ever so small degree, with that of a man who must be hounded out of his own social circle, if no worse fate is in store for him."
10110{_}4202{_}"Good gracious!"
10110{_}4203{_}cried Doris, genuinely amazed.
10110{_}4204{_}"How do you come to know all this?"
10110{_}4205{_}"I listen to the words of those qualified to speak with knowledge and authority.
10110{_}4206{_}I have mixed in varied company this past week, wholly on your account.
10110{_}4207{_}Don't be led away by the mere formalities of the opening day of the inquest.
10110{_}4208{_}The coroner deliberately shut off all real evidence except as to the cause of death.
10110{_}4209{_}On Wednesday the situation will change, and you cannot fail to be shocked by what you hear, because you will be there."
10110{_}4210{_}"I am given to understand that, even if I am called, my testimony will be of no importance."
10110{_}4211{_}"Such may be the police view.
10110{_}4212{_}Mr. Ingerman will press for a very different estimate."
10110{_}4213{_}"Has he told you that?"
10110{_}4214{_}"Yes."
10110{_}4215{_}"So, although foreman of the jury, you have not declined to hobnob with a man who is avowedly Mr. Grant's enemy?"
10110{_}4216{_}"I would hobnob with worse people if, by so doing, I might serve you."
10110{_}4217{_}Grant, "fed up," as he put it to Hart, with watching the _tete a tete_ between Doris and the chemist, sprang to his feet and went through a pantomime easy enough to follow save for one or two signs.
10110{_}4218{_}Doris held both hands aloft.
10110{_}4219{_}Well knowing that anything in the nature of a pre-arranged code would be gall and wormwood to Siddle, she explained laughingly:  "Mr. Grant signals that he and Mr. Hart are going for a walk; he wants me to accompany them.
10110{_}4220{_}But I can't, unfortunately.
10110{_}4221{_}I promised dad to help with the accounts."
10110{_}4222{_}"If you really mean what you say, my warning would seem to have fallen on deaf ears."
10110{_}4223{_}Siddle's voice was well under control, but his eyes glinted dangerously.
10110{_}4224{_}His state was that of a man torn by passion who nevertheless felt that any display of the rage possessing him would be fatal to his cause.
10110{_}4225{_}But, rather unexpectedly, Doris took fire.
10110{_}4226{_}Siddle's innuendoes and protestations were sufficiently hard to bear without the added knowledge that a ridiculous convention denied her the companionship of a man whom she loved, and who, she was beginning to believe, loved her.
10110{_}4227{_}She swept round on Siddle like a wrathful goddess.
10110{_}4228{_}"I have borne with you patiently because of the acquaintance of years, but I shall be glad if this tittle-tattle of malice and ignorance now ceases," she said proudly.
10110{_}4229{_}"Mr. Grant is my friend, and my father's friend.
10110{_}4230{_}In the first horror of the crime which has besmirched our dear little village, we both treated Mr. Grant rather badly.
10110{_}4231{_}We know better to-day.
10110{_}4232{_}Your Ingermans and your Elkins, and the rest of the busybodies gathered at the inn, may defame him as they choose, or as they dare.
10110{_}4233{_}As for me, I am his loyal comrade, and shall remain so after next Wednesday, or a score of Wednesdays.
